Important News

Mo Dehui Departs for Russia 57

Departed at 3 PM on the 21st

Scheduled to Arrive in Moscow on the 28th

A Special Train of Seven Cars with 32 Personnel

Karakhan Telegraphed to Express Welcome

Harbin Correspondence: Mo Dehui, the Plenipotentiary for the Sino-Soviet Conference, along with a delegation of 32 special committee members and secretaries, departed by special train for Russia at 3:05 PM today (21st). The special train consisted of a first-class official car for Mo and his wife, two first and second-class sleeping cars for the special committee members and secretaries, two second-class sleeping cars for the clerks, two official cars for servants and baggage, and a dining car. Mo's second son, Songheng, is also traveling by train to take up his post as the head of the Chita Consulate General, along with his family. At 2:40 PM on the 21st, Mo and his wife arrived at the station after a banquet at the Public Office with the directors of the Sino-Russian Department of the Railway Bureau. The Special Police Department's Security Team and the Railway Superintendent's Guard dispatched large teams of armed police to maintain order at the station. About several thousand people from all walks of life came to see them off. Businessmen and students from various schools in the Special District also lined up to see them off, each holding banners with slogans. Important figures present included Zhang Jinghui, the Chief Executive of the Special District; Zang Qifang, the Director of the Land Bureau of the Special District; Song Wenyu, the Mayor; Chen Kezheng, the President of the Special Court; Zhou Shouyi, the Director of the Education Department of the Special District; Ding Chao, the Garrison Commander of Binjiang; Zhao Jinlin, the Chief of Staff of the Railway Protection Army Headquarters; Yemushanafu, the Russian Director of the Eastern Railway; Danilevsky, the Director; Li Shaogeng, the Chinese Acting Director; Shen Ruilin and Zou Shangyou, the Directors, and others, totaling over a hundred people. Foreign consuls such as the Russian Consul Melnikov, the American Consul Hanson, and the Japanese Consul Yagi also attended. At 2:50 PM, Mr. Mo boarded the train, stood on the train steps, took off his hat, and greeted the crowd. At 3:05 PM, with a whistle, the special train began to move, and the well-wishers shouted slogans such as "Long Live China," "Long Live Plenipotentiary Mo," and "Smooth Sino-Russian Negotiations," accompanied by melodious military music, creating an extremely warm atmosphere. The crowd did not disperse until the train had left the station. Mo's special train will not stop at any of the small stations along the way. It will cross the border from Manzhouli Station at 12:00 AM on the 22nd, but it plans to stop for three hours at Zalanor to inspect the local coal mines to determine whether they can be restored. The mines were destroyed during the Russian unrest in 1929 and have not been restored since, and have now become a problem between the Sino-Russian railways. It is expected to arrive in Chita on March 24 and in Moscow at 10:00 AM on the 28th. The 32 people traveling with him, in addition to Mo's wife and the families of the staff, include special committee members Wang Mingchen, Li Chen, Liu Zerong, and Zhang Shouzeng; secretaries Wang Yinchuan, Wu Zesheng, Zhang Mingzhe, Tong Deshan, and Wu Run; staff members Wu Hongyou, Chen Guangqi, and Nan Wenming; and clerks Feng Jie, Dai Yunzhang, Fu Dejin, Guan Ronggui, and Ge Jingzhen. Special committee members Xu Jianping and Qian Tai telegraphed today, saying that they will arrive in Harbin in a week. Mo has instructed the diplomatic messenger to transmit Zhan Wen to Xu and Qian when they arrive in Harbin and send it to Russia. Their diplomatic passports have been processed. In addition, the Central Government has additionally assigned Lao Weixiu as a secretary, who will also come with Xu and Qian. The delegation's expenses were initially set at 52,000 yuan per month, but have recently been increased to 60,000 yuan. A batch of 50,000 yuan was remitted by the Central Government some days ago and was immediately remitted to Moscow via Liaomi.

On the evening of the 19th, the Russian Consul-General in Harbin, Melnikov, hosted a banquet for the delegation at the Eastern Railway Club. At the banquet, Mr. Melnikov said that he had received telegrams from his government and Karakhan instructing him to express their welcome to Plenipotentiary Mo. Regarding the diplomatic passports, the Russian Consul expressed his special goodwill and provided convenience for their issuance. The delegation can pick them up at any time. Various groups and organizations have been bidding farewell to Mr. Mo since the 17th, so Mr. Mo has been extremely busy these past few days. At 1:00 PM on the 20th, Mo also hosted a banquet at his private residence on Dazhi Street, Ximajiagou, inviting various newspapers, news agencies, and reporters from Tianjin and Shanghai stationed in Harbin. Mo delivered a speech at the banquet, briefly stating that he was about to leave the country and had invited everyone here for a gathering. He was honored by their presence. In terms of the long history and international situation between China and the Soviet Union, it is necessary to quickly resolve all issues. This is Mo's first trip to Russia. The Sino-Russian Conference has undergone two rounds of negotiations, and all difficulties have been eliminated. This is now his second trip to Russia, and he will continue to proceed with the same spirit as before. However, the scope of this conference has been expanded, and the responsibility is extremely heavy. He hopes that the gentlemen of the press will uphold international rights and not be afraid of the long journey, and will provide guidance at the appropriate time. Guan Hongyi, the president of the Harbin Public Gazette, replied on behalf of the press. During the banquet, Mo also told the reporters that our side already has full sincerity for this conference. As long as the Soviet Union treats us with the same attitude, the future is naturally optimistic. However, as the scope of the conference has been expanded, the three groups of the Eastern Railway, trade, and resumption of diplomatic relations will be carried out simultaneously, and the issues are complex, which is known to everyone. The matter of trade is particularly complicated, and it is difficult to complete without a longer period of research. The economic relationship between China and the Soviet Union is extremely close. Now that both sides have agreed on the principle of equal trade, every item and every matter should be sought to be fair. When discussing items and concluding treaties, we must carefully consider them. Therefore, the duration of the conference is difficult to predict. Afterwards, the host and guests dispersed in joy. (21st)

Huang Shaoxiong Comes to the Province from Hong Kong 58

To Consult with the Guangdong Authorities on the Guangxi Situation

There Are Still Rumors of Zhang, Li, and Others Resigning and Going Abroad

Guangzhou Correspondence: The Guangxi situation is proceeding peacefully. Although the two sides have been very close recently, there are still matters that need to be discussed further. Therefore, after the second batch of troops from the Eighth Route Army returned to Guangdong, the third batch remains temporarily stationed between Guiping and Guixian, guarding the key fortresses of the Dazhao River, awaiting the complete resolution of the Guangxi situation before withdrawing. It has been learned that after the withdrawal of the Yu Division of the Eighth Route Army from the front line of Binyang, Bai Chongxi of the Guangxi military has dispatched Liang Hansong's division of about 2,000 men, plus about 1,000 militiamen, to be stationed in Laibin and Qianjiang. The Guangxi military police regiment is stationed in Xiangxian. In the Nanning and Shanglin areas, Zhang Fakui, Huang Heling, and Huang Xuchu's troops of about 2,000 men are stationed separately. On the 3rd of this month, Huang Heling sent another regiment to station in Binyang. As for the attitude of Zhang Jiajun's leaders, it is rumored that Zhang, Li, and others have decided to step down and go abroad. Once the Central Government allocates funds for their travel expenses and Guangxi's post-war reconstruction, they can implement their dismissal. Huang Shaoxiong, who is mediating peace in Hong Kong, sent Xia Wei, the former commander of the Seventh Brigade of the Seventh Army, to Guangxi a few days ago to consult with Li, Bai, and others. Mr. Xia has been in Yongning for over a week, but no definitive news has been received. Zhang, Li, and Bai have also sent representatives Huang Yansheng and Li Daqun to Hong Kong to meet with Huang Shaoxiong to discuss everything. The result has been quite good. Huang Yansheng and others have long since returned to Guangxi to report on their duties. Now, Huang Shaoxiong believes that the peaceful resolution of the Guangxi situation should be realized as soon as possible, so he took a ship to the province from Hong Kong on the evening of the 18th of this month. Chen Jitang, the commander-in-chief of the Eighth Route Army, sent Chen Weizhou, the Salt Transport Commissioner, and He Luo, the director of the arsenal, to Hong Kong to welcome him. Huang arrived at the dock at about 6:00 AM on the 19th and, after exchanging greetings with the welcomers, went to the Xinya Hotel with his nephew Huang Weifang and Mr. Gong Jieyuan to stay temporarily. Then, accompanied by Du Yiqian, the chief of staff of the Eighth Route Army who came to meet him, he went directly to the Tuisi Garden in Dongshan to meet with Chen Jitang and Chen Mingshu and had breakfast in the garden. Many people from the financial circles of Guangxi and Guangdong accompanied them. At noon, Huang, accompanied by Gong Jieyuan, Wu Fan, Yang Dingzhong, and others, drove to Baiyun Mountain and toured the scenic spots of Nengren Temple and Lianquan Temple. At 3:00 PM, he returned to the Tuisi Garden to stay. In the evening, Chen Mingshu hosted a banquet to entertain him. It has been learned that Huang came here specifically to consult on the peaceful settlement of the Guangxi issue and will stay in Guangdong for a few days before returning to Hong Kong. According to Gong Jieyuan, one of Huang's close associates, the Guangxi peace is still in progress, and rumors of obstruction are purely false. Guangxi military generals Huang Xuchu and Wei Yunsong have not resigned. Wu Tingyang, the deputy director, went to Beijing this time to ask for instructions on how to settle the Guangxi situation. (March 20th)

Ministry of Finance Revises Regulations on Business Tax in Jiangsu Province 59

The "Regulations on the Collection of Business Tax in Jiangsu Province" and its implementation rules were previously passed by the 367th meeting of the Provincial Government and submitted to the Ministry of Finance for record. Various chambers of commerce in the counties, believing that the provincial regulations violated the outlines set by the Ministry, once held a meeting in Zhenjiang to discuss the matter and sent representatives to Beijing to petition for correction. It is now learned that the provincial regulations have been revised by the Ministry of Finance and submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval according to law. However, due to the sudden drop in revenue in Jiangsu Province after the abolition of the likin tax, which urgently needs to be compensated without delay, the revised regulations and implementation rules have been sent back to the Provincial Government for implementation. The revised draft is recorded as follows:

Regulations on the Collection of Business Tax in Jiangsu Province (Article 1) These regulations are in accordance with the "Outlines for Business Tax" and "Supplementary Measures" promulgated by the Ministry of Finance. (Article 2) All businesses operating within Jiangsu Province shall pay taxes in accordance with these regulations, unless otherwise stipulated by the Central Government. (Article 3) The standards for collecting business tax are provisionally set as two types: (1) Based on business turnover; (2) Based on capital. (Article 4) The business tax rates are stipulated as follows: (1) For those based on business turnover, the tax rate ranges from one per thousand to ten per thousand. (2) For those based on capital, the tax rate ranges from two per thousand to twenty per thousand. The tax rate levels mentioned above will be separately specified according to the nature of each industry. (Article 5) All businesses operating in this province, whether newly established or old, must apply for a business license by providing the following information: 1. Business type, name, and location; 2. Name, origin, and address of the business operator; 3. Business capital; 4. Estimated annual business income. The aforementioned business license shall be renewed annually without any fee. (Article 6) The tax collection agency may, when necessary, dispatch personnel to investigate and inspect the ledgers, documents, and goods used by the business operator, but must do so in conjunction with the local chamber of commerce. Without the resolution and permission of the business tax review committee, it is not allowed to remove the ledgers, documents, etc., from the inspected shop for investigation and inspection. (Article 7) If a business operator makes a false declaration, either by overreporting less or concealing information, thereby evading tax, or operates without a license, or fails to renew the license when required, in addition to being ordered to pay the taxes and obtain a license, a corresponding fine will be imposed. The penalty rules will be formulated separately. (Article 8) Businesses with operating capital of less than 500 yuan are exempt from business tax but must still apply for a business license to operate. (Article 9) For those whose tax base is based on turnover, the total annual tax payable is determined according to their estimated annual business income and tax rate. For those whose tax base is based on capital, the total annual tax payable is determined according to their capital and tax rate, divided into twelve months, and collected monthly (the monthly collection amount is one-twelfth of the annual tax amount). Receipts shall be issued by the Department of Finance. The business tax for newly opened shops shall be calculated from the month of commencement of business. (Article 10) If a business operator fails to pay the monthly tax due for more than one month, a late payment surcharge of 20% will be added. If the payment is not made for more than three months, the business may be suspended, and the tax and late payment surcharge will still be pursued. However, if the delay in payment is due to the delay of the collection agency, no late payment surcharge will be added, and no suspension of business will be imposed. (Article 11) For businesses whose types are omitted from the tax schedule but meet the nature of business tax collection, the collection agency shall propose an appropriate tax rate and submit it to the competent authority for approval and then forward it to the Ministry of Finance for review and record. (Article 12) The calculation of the capital standard amount shall be based on what is actually used for business purposes. Public reserve funds, etc., should be considered as capital. (Article 13) The calculation of business tax amount shall be based on the industry as a unit. If a household operates several industries with different tax rates, it shall be determined according to the main part of its business. (Article 14) For the sale of goods that are wholesale or bulk sales without retail, the business tax may be collected at half the rate. (Article 15) If various businesses have branches in this province, their business tax may be paid by the head office. If the head office or branch is located outside the province, it shall be remitted through the branch or head office located within the province to pay the business tax. (Article 16) Each county's business tax bureau and director shall organize a business tax review committee. (Article 17) The organization and rules of the business tax review committee will be formulated separately. (Article 18) If a business operator changes its business, adds new capital, or transfers ownership, it shall immediately report it to the competent collection agency and exchange for a new business license. (Article 19) When a business operator ceases operation, it must report to the competent collection agency within fifteen days and pay the tax due before the suspension of business. (Article 20) The collection agency shall announce the collected business tax amount monthly and compile a collection record at the end of each year, which shall be reviewed by the review committee and published with the signature of all members. (Article 21) After the implementation of the business tax, the original tooth tax, pawn tax, slaughter tax, liquor and tea house industry tax, hotel industry tax, entertainment venue industry tax, and other taxes that have not yet been collected and are the same as the business tax shall be temporarily handled according to the old regulations. After the business tax is fully implemented throughout the province, the above-mentioned original tax rates shall be changed to the business tax rates for collection. (Article 22) Detailed rules for the implementation of these regulations will be formulated separately. (Article 23) These regulations shall be reported to the Ministry of Finance for record, then promulgated and implemented.

Detailed Rules for the Implementation of the Regulations on the Collection of Business Tax in Jiangsu Province (Article 1) These detailed rules are formulated in accordance with Article 22 of the "Regulations on Business Tax in Jiangsu Province." (Article 2) The collection of business tax shall be handled by special bureaus established in counties designated by the Department of Finance as having prosperous commerce. Those that are not prosperous shall still be handled concurrently by the county government or finance bureau. (Article 3) All businesses operating within this province must apply for a business license before being allowed to operate. (Article 4) The business license mentioned in the preceding article shall be displayed by the business operator in a conspicuous place in the store for inspection. (Article 5) If a business license is lost or damaged, an application shall be submitted to the collection agency for a replacement. The old license must be returned for cancellation when a replacement is obtained. (Article 6) Business operators shall keep accounts recording the following items: 1. Detailed list of goods and raw materials purchased; 2. Detailed list of goods sold; 3. Daily detailed list of cash receipts and payments; 4. Monthly total; 5. Annual total. (Article 7) The business tax collection agency shall set up a public notice board at the entrance, which shall include the following items: 1. The business tax regulations and implementation rules, as well as announcements related to the collection methods; 2. The names of the taxpayers and the amounts of taxes and fines collected each month; 3. The daily market price of silver dollars and subsidiary coins. (Article 8) The collection of taxes shall be in national currency. Subsidiary coins may be used for fractions, converted at the market price, with uniform in and out. (Article 9) When calculating taxes, the decimals shall be rounded to the nearest li, with fractions below li rounded up if 5 or higher. (Article 10) When a business operator fills out a declaration form, if the household operates more than two types of businesses with different tax rates, it shall declare truthfully according to the main part of its business. (Article 11) The collection agency shall compile a register of business tax for each licensed business, according to the items listed in Article 5 of the Business Tax Regulations, separately by urban and rural areas, as the basis for tax collection. A copy shall be prepared and submitted to the Department of Finance for record. (Article 12) The Department of Finance, based on the reports from various county bureaus, may at any time dispatch special commissioners to conduct random inspections in conjunction with representatives of the local chamber of commerce. (Article 13) A business operator whose business is suspended due to late payment of business tax may not resume business until the taxes are paid in full. (Article 14) Business licenses and business tax receipts shall be printed and issued by the Department of Finance and stamped with the seal of the collection agency. The aforementioned business licenses and receipts shall be in triplicate, one copy for the business operator, one copy for the Department of Finance, and one copy for the collection agency. (Article 15) The term "wholesale business" in Article 14 of the Business Tax Regulations refers specifically to wholesale transactions among peers. If a business engages in both wholesale and retail, the tax amount shall still be calculated separately. (Article 16) These detailed rules shall be implemented simultaneously with the Business Tax Regulations of Jiangsu Province. (Article 17) If there are any matters not covered in these detailed rules, the Department of Finance may propose amendments to the Provincial Government at any time and report them to the Ministry of Finance for review and record. Table of Tax Standards and Rates for Business Tax in Jiangsu Province

Industry Name Tax Base Tax Rate

Goods Sales Industry Turnover One per thousand to ten per thousand

Transit Industry Turnover Two per thousand

Transportation Industry Turnover Two per thousand

Construction Industry Turnover Two per thousand

Electric Industry Turnover Two per thousand

Goods Leasing Industry Turnover Five per thousand

Photography Industry Turnover Ten per thousand

Printing, Publishing, and Books,

Stationery and Educational Supplies Industry Capital Two per thousand

Manufacturing Industry Capital Two per thousand to twenty per thousand

Warehousing Industry Capital Five per thousand

Insurance Industry Capital Twenty per thousand

Money Exchange Industry Capital Ten per thousand

Note: The liquor, tea house, hotel, and entertainment venue industries shall be handled temporarily according to the old regulations in accordance with Article 21 of these regulations. The banking, savings society, and exchange industries are all special industries and should be taxed separately by the Central Government, so they are not listed. The types and tax rates of the goods sales industry will be listed in detail below. The types and tax rates of the manufacturing industry will be listed by the Department of Finance and submitted to the Ministry for approval. Mills that have obtained a liquor business license are exempt from the tax and are not considered manufacturing. The towel industry is included in the cotton textile industry, the water work industry is included in the construction industry, the scissors are included in the ironware industry, and the tinfoil industry should be handled separately, so it is not listed. The tofu shop industry, small restaurant industry, small dish stall industry, and barber shop industry generally have capital of less than 500 yuan, so they are not listed.

Table of Labor and Tax Rates for Goods Sales Industry (Limited to the sales industry, taxed based on turnover)

Grain Industry, Firewood and Coal Industry, Oil and Salt Shop Industry: Tax rate of one per thousand for all of the above.

Cotton Industry, Bamboo and Wood Industry, Secondhand Clothing Industry, Clothing Box Industry, Yarn Industry, Tea and Paint Industry, Ironware Industry, Umbrella and Mat Industry, Comb Industry, Candle and Soap Industry, Match Industry, Silk and Satin Industry, Silk Cocoon Industry, Fruit Industry, Pastry Industry, Straw Weaving Industry, Sauce Garden Industry, Herbal Medicine Industry (If also selling ginseng and bird's nest, the tax rate is still two per thousand), Paper Industry, Fan Industry, Oil Industry (excluding edible oil), Cotton Textile Industry, Shoe, Hat, and Sock Industry, Hemp Textile Industry, North-South Goods Industry, Copper and Tinware Industry, Mountain Goods and Land Goods Industry, Brick, Tile, and Lime Industry, Pottery and Porcelain Material Industry, Packaging Paper Box Industry, Bamboo, Wood, Palm, and Rattan Ware Industry, Pickled and Preserved Fish Industry, Salted Leather, Fur, and Bone Industry, Egg Industry: Tax rate of two per thousand for all of the above.

Dye Industry, Hardware Industry, Western Medicine Industry, Lace Industry: Tax rate of five per thousand for all of the above.

Electrical Material Industry, Felt and Carpet Industry, Cement Industry, Foreign and Guangdong Goods Industry, Soda and Ice Food Industry, Candy, Tea Food, and Canned Food Industry, Sugar Industry: Tax rate of five per thousand for all of the above.

Leather Industry, Rubber Industry, Woolen Fabric Industry, Leather Goods Industry, Ginseng and Bird's Nest Industry, Antiques Industry, Tooth Filling Industry, Western Clothing Industry, Embroidery Industry, Clock and Watch and Eyeglass Industry, Jewelry and Jewelry Industry, Incense, Candle, Paper Firecracker Industry, Paper Paste Funeral Object Industry, Western-style Furniture Industry, Rosewood and Mahogany Industry, Ham Industry, Cosmetics and Art Products Industry, Phonograph Industry: Tax rate of ten per thousand for all of the above.

Note: The livestock and fresh fish industries are still subject to slaughter tax and tooth tax in accordance with Article 21 of these regulations, so they are not listed. The sand casting industry and dyeing industry are included in the manufacturing industry, and the rice milling industry is included in the grain industry.

Lu Army Encircles and Suppresses Bandits in Baodu Ridge 60

Jinan Correspondence: Han Fuju, Chairman of the Shandong Provincial Government and Commander-in-Chief of the Third Route Army, has decided to clear out Baodu Ridge, the bandits' nest of many years. He has formulated methods for encirclement and suppression. In addition to the Third Route Army's Cao Fulin, commanding Qiao Lizhi's division, and Zhan Shutang and Ning Chunxiao's two brigades, responsible for the northeast side, and Gu Liangmin's 22nd Division responsible for the Sishui route on the west side, he will also unite with Wang Jun's 7th Division in Tengxian, Ma Hongkui's 15th Route Army in Tai'an, and Chen Yaohan's 26th Division in Yizhou to implement a large-scale encirclement. Cao's 29th Division's engineering battalion, cavalry battalion, cadet battalion, and military band left Jinan for Qingzhou by train at 9:00 AM yesterday. The second train, carrying the division headquarters' eight departments and pistol battalion, led by Deputy Division Commander Xu Wenyao and Chief of Staff Wang Shiqi, also left for Qingzhou at 5:00 PM. After Gu Liangmin's 22nd Division was ordered to mobilize, the Jinpu Railway prepared four empty trains to first send the troops of Tang Yaoxun's 65th Brigade, all of whom got off at Yaocun and went to Sishui on foot via Qufu. Cao Fulin himself is scheduled to go to Qingzhou today. Han Fuju will also personally supervise the troops. The special train has been prepared, but it is not yet known whether he will go to Tengxian or Qingzhou.

Further news: The first regiment of the advance troops of the 65th Brigade, Tang Yaoxun, Kong Xiangsheng's unit, departed from Jinan southward on the first train at 1:50 PM today (23rd). The brigade headquarters and cavalry are loading onto the second train. The third and fourth trains are also being loaded and transported. Cao Fulin, commander of the 29th Division, who is responsible for commanding the northeast front, took the Jiaoji passenger train directly to Qingzhou at 12:00. Tang Yaoxun personally led the brigade staff and cavalry south on a train at 6:10 PM (23rd).

Guo Jingluan Receives Guests from All Walks of Life in Jinan 61

Jinan Correspondence: Madam Guo Jingluan, wife of Cai Gongshi, recently came to Jinan to search for the remains of Cai Gongshi for burial and to seek to recover the old Negotiation Office address to build a martyrs' shrine as a permanent memorial. At 6:00 PM on the 23rd, Madam Cai hosted a banquet at the YMCA to receive important party and government figures, representatives of various organizations, and reporters from various newspapers. Those present included Shandong Provincial Government Chairman Han Fuju, Provincial Reorganization Committee members He Siyuan, Zhang Weicun, Zhang Hongjian, Provincial Committee members Zhang Honglie, Wang Xiangrong, Wang Fangting, Jinan Mayor Wen Chenglie, Secretary-General Xing Lantian, County Reorganization Committee members Zhang Zhuxi, Li Hansan, Yu Hongyan, Public Security Bureau Chief Wang Kairu, and others, totaling over a hundred people. On the host side, in addition to Madam Cai, Cai Yushan and Guo Ruheng were responsible for entertaining everyone. During the banquet, He Siyuan first introduced Han Chunru (an old worker at the former Negotiation Office whose son was a secretary at the Negotiation Office and was killed at the same time as Cai Gongshi; Han was spared because he went to the city to post slogans), Xin Changsheng (a handyman at the former Negotiation Office who was tied up with Cai Gongshi by the Japanese and temporarily escaped, shot five times by Japanese soldiers but not killed), and Zhang Hanru (Cai Gongshi's bodyguard who escaped from a gap in the wall when Cai was brutally killed by the Japanese, hit by several bullets, and fortunately, a Chinese man pushing water, ordered him to pose as a water carrier, thus avoiding death). The three men reported on the tragic circumstances of Cai Gongshi's death, with tears in their eyes. Next, Madam Cai delivered a speech, saying briefly that she was extremely honored by the presence of everyone. This time, Jingluan came to Jinan to search for the remains of Martyr Cai and to discuss building a martyrs' shrine as a permanent memorial. Four years have passed since the tragedy occurred. Jingluan organized the Gongshi School in Shanghai and went to Nanyang to raise over 300,000 yuan, which was fortunately established. She also suffered from repeated discomfort and was sick, so she came only today. Because she is unfamiliar with the people and place, she hopes that everyone will give her guidance and assistance. Next, Guo Yumin read out the proposed opinions drafted by Madam Cai (the original text is very long and omitted). Finally, He Siyuan and Han Fuju delivered speeches one after another, generally saying that the May 3rd Massacre and Martyr Cai's martyrdom were a great humiliation to our country, and the people of the country were all indignant. Today, being entertained by Madam Cai, they felt extremely ashamed. Martyr Cai's death is of great importance to the party and the country, and how to properly handle it is enough to comfort his heroic soul. They highly agreed with the opinions put forward by Madam Cai, but it is best to nominate a few people to formulate detailed measures. Therefore, He Siyuan, Zhang Weicun, Wen Chenglie, Chen Jiadong (Director of the Stamp, Tobacco, and Alcohol Tax Bureau), Cui Shijie (Jiaoji Railway Committee Member), Wang Kairu, Lu Tingzhuan (President of the Bank of Communications), Xing Lantian, and Madam Cai were nominated as eleven members to form a committee, scheduled to meet at the Jiaoji Hotel at 2:00 PM on the 24th to study everything. At 9:00 PM, a photo was taken and they dispersed (23rd).

Resolution of Chen Yuxi's Injury Case 62

Jinan Correspondence: On the 12th of this month, when the Jinan Municipal Government held a memorial service for the death of Sun Yat-sen, Chen Yuxi, a female student from a girls' middle school, was injured by a military vehicle while attending the meeting (as reported in previous newspapers). It is reported that Chen Yuxi's injured foot bone was broken in two places and has now been reattached by a doctor. Her life is no longer in danger, but she may be crippled and not return to her original condition after recovery. Regarding the resolution method, because Chen Yuxi's father, Chen Boyan, is a Jinan salt merchant, he has repeatedly stated that he does not want any consolation money or medical expenses. Therefore, the school recently sent a letter to the Public Security Bureau, only requesting seven items, deleting the consolation money item. The official letter said: Our school organized a team to go to the Municipal Government on March 12 to participate in the sixth anniversary memorial meeting for the death of Sun Yat-sen. Student Chen Yuxi was injured by military vehicle No. 6. The matter has been communicated in the record. As for the various matters that should be handled afterwards, your bureau chief has accepted the handling of the matter, for which we are very grateful. In addition to listing the items to be handled one by one, we hereby inform you and hope you will investigate and handle them and give a reply. A total of seven conditions are attached: (1) The Public Security Bureau should issue a notice that vehicles of any business or any organization should not be driven quickly to avoid causing disasters. (2) The driver of the car should be severely punished according to the law. (3) Prevent the recurrence of similar incidents in the future. (4) The owner of the car that caused the accident should apologize to the family of the injured student. (5) Punish the police officer on duty at the scene of the accident. (6) Any car should not be driven into the meeting place when holding a citizens' congress. (7) Cars should not rush into the team when encountering a citizens' congress marching in formation. After receiving the letter, the Public Security Bureau is deliberating. Chairman of the Provincial Government Han Fuju returned to Jinan from inspecting northern Shandong and heard about the matter. He attached great importance to it and immediately summoned Jinan Mayor Wen Chenglie to inquire about everything. After Wen reported in detail, Han immediately instructed Wen to order the Public Security Bureau to send the driver of military vehicle No. 6 to the local court immediately to be punished according to law and allocated 200 yuan to Chen for medical expenses, ordering Wen to personally send it to Chen's family and express condolences. The municipal government has now formulated seven rules for drivers of motor vehicles to pay attention to and announced their implementation. It is expected that this case can be considered resolved (22nd).

After the Qingdao Indigenous Product Merchants' Strike 63

Sharp Decline in Customs and Port Bureau Revenue

More Than Ten Thousand Dockworkers Unemployed

Qingdao Correspondence: Qingdao's local product merchants were unable to bear the inspection fees charged by the Commodity Inspection Bureau for domestically sold peanut kernels and peanut oil, so they collectively went on strike on the 17th and sent representatives to petition the party and government agencies. Both the party and government sides believed that the strike of the local product merchants had a great impact on the market, and the financial and labor sectors were also severely hit. If a solution was not found quickly, the city's commerce would be unbearable. The Party Headquarters specially sent the two members, Hou Shenglin and Qin Yiwen, and the municipal government sent Secretary-General Hu Jiafeng. Yesterday (21st), they went to the Commodity Inspection Bureau together to discuss mediation methods with the Bureau Chief, Mou Junde. The discussion lasted for two hours, but no agreement was reached. It is reported that the local product merchants are very firm in their attitude in this strike. If they do not achieve their goals, they will find a way to export through Yantai and Longkou to avoid inspection and fees. Since the strike of the local product merchants, the market has been greatly affected. The first to bear the brunt are the general workers and shipping companies, followed by the customs and port bureaus. Because the merchants have stopped transporting goods, Butterfield & Swire has telegraphed foreign ships to temporarily stop coming to Qingdao. Jardine Matheson & Co. is also planning to follow Butterfield & Swire's example because the strike has no end in sight. During the strike, there are already more than 10,000 unemployed dockworkers. These workers rely on loading and unloading cargo ships for a living. Once unemployed, they face the risk of freezing and starvation. The Qingdao Customs and Port Bureau have seen a sharp decline in various tax revenues in recent days because local products have all stopped being transported. Qingdao's exports of local products are mainly peanut kernels and peanut oil. Since the strike on the 17th, peanut kernels and peanut oil have fallen sharply in price due to lack of sales. Peanut kernels were around 11.5 yuan before the strike and have fallen to below 10.02 yuan in recent days. Peanut oil was around 23 yuan before the strike and has fallen to below 21 yuan in recent days. The Shanghai Exchange has also been greatly affected and has fallen from more than forty taels to just over thirty-seven taels in recent days. If the strike problem is not resolved quickly, it is feared that all industries will suffer a panic (March 22nd).

Bandit Alarms in Fujian Province Recently 64

Lu's Troops Defect One After Another

Suburbs Harassed by Bandits

Fuzhou Correspondence: In Fujian Province in recent years, there have been repeated incidents of mutinies by stationed troops. For example, the two companies of Yu and Zhuo in Qian Yuguang's troops and Chen Heling in Zhang Ziming's troops are notable. Recently, the two battalions of Rao Kairu and Wei Jianxin in Lu Xingbang's troops also mutinied. After Lu pursued and suppressed them, they fled to Shunchang. Lu has now telegraphed the Provincial Government not to allow the Shunchang County Magistrate to accept them. Recently, Huang Ruobai, Director of the Business Tax Preparation Office in Shaowu, telegraphed the Provincial Government, saying that on the 18th, the troops stationed in Guangze under Ma mutinied, and the County Magistrate Li Dai was killed. The order is in chaos. At the same time, the section chief of the county also had the same report and asked for telegrams to various armies to suppress the bandits and to send personnel to handle county affairs. It is found that Ma's troops should be Ma Hongzao's battalion under Lu Xinming, and Lu Xinming telegraphed the province yesterday that he had entered Liancheng. At present, it is still impossible to know the truth. The villages northwest of Fuzhou have recently heard of bandit alarms one after another. On the evening of the 20th, Meiting Township, six or seven li away from the West City, was looted by the bandits under He Enniu and Li Yirun. The villagers, hearing the news, fled in advance. The troops rushed overnight, but the bandits had fled far away. On the morning of the 21st, dozens of farmers held flags and petitioned the Provincial Government, hoping that they would send capable troops to the area to station and maintain security (March 21st).

Deng Xihou Telegraphs the Cruel Situation of the Gansu Bandits 65

Requesting the Central Government to Dispatch Troops for Suppression

His Troops Will Be Stationed on the Border Waiting for Orders

Deng Xihou, the General Commander of the Fourteenth Route Army, recently telegraphed the headquarters, reporting in detail the bandit army's disturbances in the Chuanbian (Sichuan border region), Shaanxi, and Gansu areas. The original telegram stated: "My troops are stationed in Songmao, close to southern Longnan. In recent years, we have been protecting merchants and maintaining transportation between Sichuan and Gansu, making it convenient for travelers. Recently, taking advantage of the military unrest, bandit leaders such as Ma Tingxian gathered bandits into an army and arbitrarily appointed military commanders and commanders-in-chief, committing all kinds of atrocities in southern Longnan. After the defeat of the rebellious Feng (Yuxiang), the defeated soldiers joined them, intensifying the devastation. Local organizations and people have repeatedly pleaded for the dispatch of troops for rescue, and their descriptions of the atrocities are beyond imagination. The bandit Ma Tingxian and his subordinates, military commanders Ma Zhong, Wang Zhanlin, Han Jin, Ma Rucang, etc., are all of cruel nature and intent on slaughter. When attacking southern Shaanxi, they carried out massacres in every city they captured. Young women, girls, and young boys were all raped. Their methods of killing men involved breaking their limbs, abandoning them by the roadside, where they would groan for three or four days without dying. Or they would cut open their abdomens and stuff them with grass to feed cattle and horses, or burn copper and iron instruments to brand their faces to extort money. Women were gathered in groups of dozens and raped by bandits until death to satisfy their desires. Others were placed in the Seven-Room Building in Tianshui for the bandit leaders to compete in debauchery. If not used, they were tied up, and boiling oil was poured into their vaginas, or burning coals were inserted into their genitals. As for killing infants, they were placed on the ground between two door panels, and four or five people would repeatedly trample them until their brains and intestines were crushed. The elderly and weak were locked in dark rooms, and soldiers would enter and kill them indiscriminately until they were exhausted. They enjoyed this game every day. They even dug several mass graves outside Tianshui City and buried men, women, old, and young alive in them. In the Dongyao cave in Dingxi, more than 8,000 people were buried alive. The number of people killed determined the rank of officials. In these months, the number of people slaughtered, burned to death, and raped to death is countless. The number of those who committed suicide by jumping into wells, taking poison, or hanging themselves from the city walls due to rape is even greater. The most cruel act was Wang Zhanlin's capture of Lixian County. The people all defended themselves. After the city was captured, he ordered the city to be cleansed, and except for a few women who were captured, no one, young or old, in the entire city was spared. His brutal acts far exceeded those of Zhang Xianzhong, and it was a cruelty unprecedented in history. Your Excellency, please have pity on the small people trapped in misery and order me to lead my troops to clear the countryside and maintain the border. On the one hand, I will report in detail the situation of entering Gansu to clear the bandits and request instructions on strategy. On the other hand, I will also send personnel to the bandits'驻地, explaining the advantages and disadvantages, hoping that they will correct their mistakes, return to the right path, and follow the national law. However, the bandits could not be reasoned with and even shot all the representatives I sent. Taking advantage of our lack of preparation, they colluded with Xiao Jitang, who claimed to be the commander of the Anti-Rebel Army, and led their gangs Bai Yun, etc., to launch a large-scale attack. The Wencun and Bicun locations were repeatedly in danger. After a hard battle for more than ten days by my troops, the bandit troops were finally repelled, and the residents near Wenxian County were slightly relieved. Unexpectedly, the bandits' ambitions were not curbed, and they frequently came to loot. The county people are terrified, fearing only the departure of my troops, and they wept and begged us to stay. Because Gansu Province also belongs to the national territory and is also part of the Chinese people, how can we discriminate against those who are crying under the knife without saving them? The bandits are so rampant that they are not only a pain for the people of Sichuan and Gansu but will also become a concern for the central government's westward gaze. Therefore, I especially reveal the truth and earnestly request the central government to first send personnel to Gansu to investigate the truth of the suffering of the Gansu people so that rumors will cease. On one hand, mobilize several divisions of the national army to open up Shaanxi and supervise the suppression. My troops will be stationed on the border waiting for orders. If the bandit troubles can be eliminated, it will not only be a blessing for the people of Gansu, but also the merchants and travelers on the Sichuan border will benefit from it."

The Shanxi Provincial Party Department Telegraphs Again Requesting the Reorganization of the Ordnance Factory 66

Advocating for its Conversion into a Machinery and Rail Manufacturing Plant

Taiyuan Correspondence: Although the central government and the Northeast authorities have sent personnel to inspect the reorganization of the Shanxi Ordnance Factory, a definite solution has not yet been determined. Recently, with the closure of the headquarters, the factory's funding has no source. Although the public unanimously advocates for converting it into a people's livelihood institution, there is still no effect. The Provincial Party Department specially telegraphed the central government again yesterday, requesting the factory to be converted into agricultural and industrial machinery and Datong-Puzhou railway rail manufacturing plants to meet the public's opinion and eliminate the source of trouble. The original text is as follows: "To the Nanjing Central Executive Committee, Your Excellencies: We have successively telegraphed to you the disadvantages of the Shanxi Ordnance Factory and the reasons why it should be converted into a productive enterprise. Now, based on the Premier's industrial plan and the needs of Shanxi's current environment, we further clarify the matter. If China wants to develop agriculture to enrich the people, then improving agricultural tools is essential. The Premier saw this early on, so in the industrial plan, there was a proposal to set up an agricultural tool manufacturing plant. Now, the factory's machinery can be used to manufacture new-style agricultural tools for improving agriculture in Shanxi and land reclamation in the Northwest, which will be of unlimited benefit. This is the first point. Shanxi is rich in mineral resources, surpassing the whole country, but it lacks mining machinery and relies mostly on human labor, which is time-consuming and laborious and difficult to achieve complete results. Now, the factory's machinery can be used to transform mining machinery to develop Shanxi's coal and iron to relieve people's livelihood and promote the future construction of northern ports. This is the second point. Our country's industry is still in the handicraft era. To revitalize it in the future, the first step is to use machinery. Now, the factory's machinery can be used to manufacture various industrial machines, and the various industrial plans in the second part of the Premier's industrial plan can be gradually implemented. The problem of people's livelihood can also be easily solved. This is the third point. The construction of the Datong-Puzhou Railway has been proposed for a long time, but it has not yet been realized because of the limitation of capital. It is difficult to purchase machinery, and there are no funds to purchase equipment. In today's environment of poor people and exhausted wealth, if even a rail or a spike must be purchased from abroad, it can be asserted that it is not easy to build. However, this road is of great importance to the development of commerce, mining, and industry, the progress of culture and education in Shanxi Province, and it is urgent to repair it. Now, the Datong-Puzhou Railway machinery and rails can be manufactured using the factory, and the cost of the iron-producing area in Shanxi can be reduced, and the process will be easier. It will also be a considerable supplement to the future construction of various routes in the fourth part of the fourth plan of the Premier's industrial plan. This is the fourth point. To sum up the above points, converting the factory into a manufacturing plant for agricultural tools, mining machinery, various industrial machinery, Datong-Puzhou Railway machinery, and rails is the most urgent task today. As for whether the factories should be manufactured separately or merged into one factory, the planning can be entrusted to experts in the future. We hereby reiterate the previous request based on the environment of Shanxi and the current needs of our country. We implore your council to transfer it to the National Government and order the Shanxi Provincial Government to handle it immediately, and we will be waiting for orders with great anticipation."

Local Correspondence

Taicang 67

The Mao City Township Robbery Case: At the home of farmer Li Xiaodi in the Er Tu area of the Thirteenth Du in the old Mao City Township of this county, more than 20 bandits speaking with a Jiangbei accent broke into the house late at night on the 23rd, tied up the Li family, both men and women, and looted at will. They stole 80 yuan in cash and 16 shi of white rice. Later, they went to the home of farmer Zhang Aisheng and looted more than 10 yuan in cash, 4 shi of white rice, as well as clothes and silver ornaments. After four hours, they left with a howl. Li and others have reported to the county to request their arrest.

Qingpu 68

The West Bay Village Robbery and Injury Case: Zhu of West Bay Village outside the North Gate of this county held a wedding for his son the other day, and the congratulatory guests were plentiful and lively. Unexpectedly, at about 8 p.m., dozens of bandits suddenly came and rushed in, blocking the way of the male and female guests and looting at will, resulting in heavy losses. Zhu and his son were both injured by the bandits and have gone to Shanghai for treatment.

Suspects in the Xiaogang Robbery Case Arrested: The Xiaogang Robbery Case near Tailai Bridge in the county's first district has not yet been solved. The other day, Shen Jinghua, the director of the County Public Security Bureau, and Wang Yulin, the captain of the Water Patrol Team, led police officers and informants to search the Zhongshan and Dahua Paper Mills in Zhujiajiao East Market. The informant identified Ding Chengzhang, the owner of the Zhongshan Mill, and the female worker Li Guafu, etc., as major suspects, and they were arrested by the police. That night, they were detained at the Zhujiajiao Public Security Bureau. Except for the owner of the Zhongshan Mill, who was released on bail temporarily, the rest were escorted to the Qingpu County Government for further investigation.

Suzhou 69

Former Pizhou County Magistrate Arrested in Suzhou: Wang Jiatian, the former magistrate of Pizhou County, was impeached by Wang Xipeng and Chen Kuiyi, citizens of the county, to the Provincial Government and the High Court for owing 36,000 yuan in public funds. The Provincial Government issued an order to dismiss him. Wang did not clear up the handover when he left office, and the Provincial Government issued an arrest warrant. As for Wang Xipeng and others suing in the High Court, Wang Jiatian was suspected of counter-revolution. Prosecutor Zhu Jun of the High Procuratorate has repeatedly summoned him for investigation and released him on bail. Wang Xipeng and others telegraphed the High Procuratorate again on the 23rd of this month, requesting that it be handled according to law. Prosecutor Zhu of the High Procuratorate originally scheduled to summon Wang Jiatian to the case for investigation on the afternoon of the 24th. After Wang received the summons, he arrived in Suzhou the next day. When he arrived at the case for interrogation on the afternoon of the 24th, he was still released on bail. Unexpectedly, the original accusers, Wang Xipeng and Chen Kuiyi, learned of the investigation date and followed him to Suzhou. When Wang Jiatian left the court at the gate of the High Court on the afternoon of the 24th, they stepped forward and grabbed Wang. Liu Fengshan, the policeman on duty at the station, saw this and inquired about the cause and effect, so he took them to the station. After a brief interrogation by Fang Ziqing, a patrol officer from the Fifth Branch of the Second Bureau, he immediately prepared a document and sent it to the Second Branch for transfer to the Public Security Bureau for verification.

Gao Ying's Opium Trafficking Case Opens Today: Gao Ying, the former Vice Consul in San Francisco, his wife Gao Liao, and his secretary Sun Yuan, appealed to the Supreme Court against the second-instance judgment of the High Court for trafficking in opium. The Supreme Court ruled on October 6 last year that the appeal of Gao Liao was dismissed, and the appeal of Gao Ying and Sun Yuan was sent back to the High Court for a retrial. After deliberation, the case was accepted by Lin Dawen, the presiding judge of the First Criminal Court. Judge Lin immediately presented the case to the ministry for an electric transfer of evidence. He has already replied in the last month and scheduled a hearing for today (26th) at 1 p.m. It is said that the witnesses summoned are Chen Sheng, etc. Gao Liao has also received a summons, but Gao Liao's hemoptysis has not yet recovered and she cannot get out of bed, so it is feared that she will not be able to attend the court hearing today.

Bandits Rampant in Taihu Lake Again: Yesterday, five or six bandit ships with about 100 bandits suddenly arrived in the Hemantang area of Taihu Lake and roamed around Dagong Mountain and Xiaogong Mountain. The various township chiefs have jointly submitted a report to the county government, requesting that a team be dispatched to the countryside to suppress the bandits immediately. After receiving the report, County Magistrate Huang telegraphed the third district of the Water Public Security Bureau and ordered the police team to rush to suppress the bandits. He also telegraphed the Pacification Superintendent's Office, requesting that a team be dispatched to Suzhou for joint suppression.

Changshu 70

They broke into the house and robbed them of a leather robe and several hundred yuan in cash. It was heard that the bandits tied up Gong's wife before entering the house to rob. Because of this, it was heard that the bandits all had a fishy smell on their hands. After the incident, it was investigated that the case may have been committed by fishermen.

Wuxi 71

He immediately led more than ten detectives from Yu to Wuxi and went to the address to arrest them at about 5 a.m. yesterday. The Liu brothers were arrested together and immediately taken by car to Suzhou, where they transferred to the Changshu ship to return to Yu for interrogation.

Dangkou Power Plant to be Merged with Suzhou: The Yepiyi Electric Power Plant in Dangkou Town, Nanyan City, which belongs to the county, was founded by Hua Ze alone with a capital of 50,000 yuan. It supplies electricity to the whole town and Ganlu Town, and the poles and lines are planted to Jiejing Bridge. Recently, the operating rights of the plant have been decided to be merged with the Suzhou Electric Power Plant for a price of 45,000 yuan, with 33,000 yuan paid in advance, and the case has been filed with the Wuxian County Government.

The Rush to Establish Relief Homes: The county government convened a meeting to prepare for the establishment of the county relief home yesterday. The resolutions are as follows: (1) How should the funds for the relief home be allocated? It was resolved to allocate and apply the 300 yuan per month that has been included in the county's local expenditure budget for the nineteenth year. (2) The location of the relief home was resolved by the president and vice president to discuss and decide. (3) What organizations should be set up in the relief home? It was resolved that the medical center should be reorganized from Hengshantang according to the original plan, the nursery should be reorganized from Tongrentang and Yuyingtang, the disabled center should be attached to the people's vocational training center, and the nursing home should be reorganized from Pujitang. (4) The date of establishment of the relief home was resolved to be determined by the president and vice president. (5) How should the short funds for the Pingsuo be compensated? It was resolved to include the expenses of the institute in the local expenditure budget for the twentieth year at 300 yuan per month, and the insufficient amount will be discussed separately.

Nantong 72

The Rampant Situation of the River Pirates in Northern Jiangsu: After the fighting between the river pirates gathered along the coast of Northern Jiangsu, there are now three factions, Yan Zhenling, Zhong Zhaokui, and Fu Damaizi, with more than 500 bandits. Lusi is their lair. In addition to hijacking merchant ships, the bandits also窜 to various places along the river and sea to kidnap and extort ransoms. Recently, with the fishing season approaching in the counties of Tong, Ru, Hai, and Qi, the bandits have been demanding flag license fees from fishermen. This year, each ship must pay 120 yuan per month. Because the bandits are divided into three factions, they demand money at the same time, and the fishermen cannot afford it. They dare not go to sea. The Gu Yu peak season is coming soon, which is especially important to the fishermen's livelihood for the year. They have sent representatives to appeal to the province for the rapid implementation of measures to protect the fishing season.

Huaihai Industrial Bank Revived: Huaihai Industrial Bank was founded in 1920. Later, due to excessive lending in the salt reclamation sector, it was unable to maneuver, which led to a standstill. Now, Li Qiqing and Zhang Xiaoruo are raising new shares to continue operations. Chen Guansan has been appointed as the president.

After his mother's funeral, his concubine died of the plague. Before the concubine's funeral was over,

six or seven bandits broke into his house over the wall in the middle of the night the other day. They forbade him to make a sound and searched all the soft silver foreign coins in the house. Before leaving, they also tied Chen Yinlu and his son (only four years old).

Shangyu 74

Major Fire Outside the East Gate: At about 2 p.m. on the 22nd of this month, Ge Ni of the Xu family in Xujialong outside the East Gate was careless. Because the place was in the open field, the wind was strong, and it soon spread to the eight families of Ge Shufeng, Chen Atu, Xuan Jisheng, Ge Jiren, Ge Fengxiang, Ge Jinyan, Ge Zhixian, and Ge Jincai. After more than two hours of rescue by water dragons inside and outside the city, the fire was extinguished. It was heard that the cause of the fire was that Ge Ni (an old woman of eighty who lived alone) picked up bamboo leaves and lit a fire in the attic, which spread to the bed curtains. Among them, the losses of Ge Fengxiang and Ge Jiren were the greatest. The whole family lived in Shanghai, and the equipment in the house was locked, and there was no way to take it out in a hurry, and it was all destroyed by the fire. This battle destroyed a total of fifteen buildings and seven flat houses, with losses amounting to more than 30,000 yuan.

Special Item

Explanatory Memorandum on the Proposal to Reduce Provincial Areas 75

Our country's provincial system originated in the Yuan Dynasty. It was not intended to be profound, but only to facilitate military affairs and was a temporary arrangement. The Ming and Qing dynasties followed it, and the Republic of China followed the old system, which has become cumbersome and extensive. People have discussed it in great detail. This is indeed an important issue in our country's administrative system. Now that the military has been pacified and political tutelage has begun, if we want to improve administrative efficiency, we must re-examine the provincial areas and reduce the area. The reasons are listed as follows:

First, the territory is vast. The size of our country's provinces is unmatched in the world. Hebei Province is larger than the sum of England and Wales. Sichuan Province is larger than the three islands of Japan. Compared with Zhejiang Province, which has a very small area, it is still larger than Belgium and the Netherlands. Even a county's territory is larger than that of a country in Europe or Central and South America. The whip is too long to reach, and governance is crude. Although the provincial government has the power to command and supervise, in fact, the issuance of orders relies on a piece of paper. Whether the counties implement the orders is unknown. The results of the implementation are even more unknowable. The advantages and disadvantages of the place, the economic decline, are even more ignorant. The provincial government suffers from the lack of effective command, and the counties feel that the feelings of the lower levels cannot reach the upper levels. Therefore, even if there are good plans for various important policies such as autonomy, education, industry, and transportation, they cannot be implemented. This is one reason why the provincial area must be reduced.

Second, transportation is congested. Although our country's culture is very old, the development of material civilization is very late. In terms of transportation, except for a few provinces in the northeast and southeast, which have railways that can be reached, or also have the advantage of shipping, the 28 provinces and Mongolia and Tibet have few railways. In the northwest, such as Gansu, Qinghai, and Ningxia, and in the southwest, such as Sichuan, Xikang, Guizhou, and Guangxi, there is not even a foot of railway, and there are few rivers. Mongolia and Tibet are even more isolated. The means of transportation rely solely on the ancient mule carts, camels, sedan chairs, and civilian ships. Because of the vastness of the territory and the many mountains, it takes four or five days or ten days from the county to the countryside, and it takes months from the province to the county. Even if the government has the determination to work hard, it will never have the effect of making arms and fingers work effectively. Compared with the civilized countries of the world, where government orders are urgent, and transportation arrives in the morning and evening, it is like heaven and earth. This is the second reason why the provincial area must be reduced.

Third, the situations are different. Within a province, languages are not common, desires are different, customs are different, interests are different, and economies are suspended. In the same province, the east, west, north, and south, interests run counter to each other. Therefore, if the provincial government implements policies uniformly, there will be sighs of cold, heat, rain, and rain. If it adapts to local conditions, it will feel the pain of cutting feet to fit shoes. This is the third reason why the provincial area must be reduced.

Fourth, the boundaries are too deep. The people of our country have a deep-rooted view of boundaries, and provincial boundaries are one aspect. Since the Republic of China, this trend has not changed. When an organ changes a long history, many fellow villagers celebrate. If provincial籍 are different, even talented people will be rejected. This is not only true of politics, but also in commerce and society. The boundaries are clear, like a chasm. Those who argue that the Chinese people's intelligence and talent are no less than those of Westerners, but lack a spirit of cooperation, thus reducing the efficiency of doing things, attribute the lack of cooperative spirit to provincial boundaries. This is the fourth reason why the provincial area must be reduced.

Fifth, military separatism. The vastness of the territory and the congestion of transportation have been described above. Unfortunately, ambitious people arise, holding military power, residing in the provincial capital. The military strength and wealth of a province are equal to that of a country in the world, so it can confront the central government. The authority of the central government loses its control. For the past 20 years, warlord separatism and internal strife have been cyclical, plunging the people into misery, and being a great obstacle to the national revolution, not or not because of this. Now that the disease is settled, it is necessary to change the strings and change the chapter. This is the fifth reason why the provincial area must be reduced.

The above reasons, the first four are chronic diseases, and the latter one is a new disease. The first four are ill with numbness, and the latter one is ill in the heart. In short, chronic diseases, new diseases, numbness, and diseases in the heart all need to be treated as one. The humble view of the pivot is that reducing the provincial area is a good prescription for the symptoms. In the past, France suffered from being too large, difficult to govern, too deep in boundaries, and military separatism, which was roughly the same as the situation in our country today. During the Great Revolution, it resolutely abolished 40 provinces and changed them to 87 states. As a result, governance was meticulous, and the meridians were connected. It has continued to this day, and all wastes have been raised. The party is the only party for revolution and nation-building. Today is the beginning of the implementation of political tutelage. With the spirit of decades of struggle, we seek the reform of the political region, so that the central government and the provinces can have equal power, and the local area can implement autonomy. There is no other way. The method is to reduce the area of the provinces, divide each province into two or three, examine the topography of mountains and rivers, convenient transportation, financial surpluses and deficits, population density, and economic abundance as the criteria for division, so as to make adjustments properly, make orders agile, cut long and make up for short, and do not have partial dryness, so as to meet the requirements of the times and plan the improvement of politics. Furthermore, the national government affairs are numerous and mixed. If it is appropriate to concentrate power in the central government, if it is appropriate to decentralize power to the provinces, if it is appropriate for the central government and the provinces to co-govern and cooperate, our country's central and local powers are not divided, which is a major disease of political image. Between the two, there are often disagreements or mutual evasion. Disagreements and evasions are caused by all kinds of abuses, and government affairs are abandoned. Some say that the division of such powers is an important issue in the future constitution, and there is no place for branch changes. They do not know the difference between the constitution and the non-constitution, not in whether the central and local powers are divided, but in whether the division is fixed. It is recorded in the constitution, so it has robustness. If it is amended, it must go through serious procedures. If it is not recorded in the constitution, it has fluidity and can be modified at any time in consideration of the situation and political image. This should also be stipulated at the same time as the provincial area reduction plan. I hereby give a supplementary explanation to the right, Wu Chaochu.
