Local News

The Gold Profit Source Case Negotiations Gradually Become Serious 76

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company (CMSNC) Has Requested the Government

to Cancel the Deed of the Sande (Three Virtues) Church

If the Sande Church Does Not Realize the Situation Very Soon,

It Should Bear Full Responsibility for Any Accidents That Occur

Regarding the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Gold Profit Source case, because of the Sande Church's Father Hsia-ch'i's (Xavier) rude attitude, breaking promises and reneging on agreements, and withdrawing its agreement to sell the pier to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, after the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company sent a letter, in addition to replying to the Sande Church, it also sent a letter to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to seriously negotiate. If the church still wants to hoard, please ask the government to check the files and fundamentally cancel the deed held by the church. The details of each situation are recorded as follows:

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Letter to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs: Respectfully informing you that our company and the French Catholic Sande Church have had disputes over land rental, and have repeatedly been involved in litigation, mediation, negotiation, and arbitration. Last December, we sent a letter to your ministry requesting assistance in negotiations and sending a note to the French envoy, ordering the French consul in Shanghai to strictly order the Sande Church to quickly resolve the matter. Our company believes that in this matter, based on diplomatic history, we are justified and will never lightly abandon our national rights or submit to the biased judgment of the French Concession Mixed Court. Furthermore, due to the discovery of new evidence, we have already filed a retrial with the French Concession Mixed Court. On our company's side, we have already determined our steps, and we must either continue the lease quickly or purchase it at a fair price. However, the French Consul General expressed sincerity and intended to maintain Sino-French relations, secretly preventing the Mixed Court from executing the judgment, and exerted extraordinary effort. In addition, prominent Shanghai gentry and merchants also mediated, hoping to reach a peaceful resolution. Our company, in view of the kindness of the outside world and the sincerity of the French Consul, did not want to immediately take extreme measures, and waited quietly for mediation. Recently, according to the mediators and the French Consul, they said that they had reached an agreement with the Sande Church, and our company could purchase the land at a fair price. They also instructed our company to send someone to negotiate the purchase price with the Sande Church. Our company, respecting the opinions of the mediators and the French Consul, immediately sent attorney Kao Shuo, who had previously served as an arbitrator, to formally represent our company and personally went to the Sande Church to meet with the responsible father. Unexpectedly, the father expressed that he was still stubborn and still insisted on his high price of 330,000 taels, with little concession, resulting in no result. Our company, forced to do so, turned to inquire with the mediators, who were surprised by the father's fickleness and only urged us to send a letter to the church to counteroffer. Our company, respecting the public opinion, sent a public letter to the church a few days ago, counteroffering 200,000 taels to purchase the land. The church has not yet replied, but based on our company's observation, the church may not have genuine remorse. If it still deliberately hoards and does not concede, our company will have to, based on diplomatic history and the original text of the contract, announce to the public and let the people judge right and wrong. At the same time, we will request the government to check the files and fundamentally cancel the deed held by the church. At that time, if the public, aroused by justice, attacks the church, forcibly seizes property, unreasonably invalidates the contract, and exposes all acts of engaging in business for profit under the guise of missionary work, and an accident occurs, harming Sino-French relations, then the responsibility for opening the gap should be borne by the church, and it cannot be said that our company intentionally provoked the incident improperly. After all, the diplomatic history of the previous Qing Dynasty for eight years does not allow the church to recklessly ignore it. Therefore, we specially request your ministry to send a note to the French envoy in China, ordering the French Consul in Shanghai to strictly order the Sande Church to fulfill the provisions of the land deed, not to hinder our company's use, continue the lease, or respect the mediator's arbitration and sell at a fair price, so as to avoid inciting a storm and affecting diplomatic relations. If your ministry believes that sending a note to the French envoy is too complicated, please inform your office in Shanghai to advise the French Consul and supervise the church to quickly and fairly settle the matter, and not to be stubborn again. Fortunately, the French Consul has expressed goodwill from the beginning and has repeatedly acted as a mediator. Now, if we issue a serious warning, he may use it as an excuse to force the church. The matter concerns national rights and national navigation. We earnestly request your ministry to vigorously preside over it, hoping for an early resolution and to achieve a final victory, then our gratitude will be boundless. All the details of the case and the key points for negotiation are hereby communicated. We hope you will investigate and reply. Respectfully addressed to Minister Wang of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. (March 19th)

Kao Shuo's Report to General Manager Li: Respectfully informing you that I have received a letter from attorney Bahe on March 18th, stating that according to the Sande Church, your attorney's letter to Father Hsia-ch'i, the manager of the church, on the 17th of this month, has been reviewed, and he has been entrusted to reply as follows: According to the letter, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company is willing to use 200,000 Shanghai Common Regulations silver dollars to purchase all the rights to the pier and appurtenances of the Gold Profit Source pier, French Register A, No. 69. After investigation, the price offered differs by 190,000 taels from the price quoted by our client on November 3, 1930. Our client believes that it is difficult to approach the matter and there is no need to continue negotiations. Therefore, we specially convey this formally on their behalf. All of our client's price of 390,000 taels for selling the land of French Register A, No. 69 to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company on November 3, 1930, is now unconditionally withdrawn. Please investigate and inform the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. I hereby request your approval for handling. Furthermore, on the 13th of this month, I was ordered to represent you and accompanied Mr. Zhang Ji-xian, a member of the French Municipal Council, to the father's residence to discuss the purchase price of the land. We went sincerely, with the aim of settling the matter. We hoped that the case would be concluded soon. However, the father spoke rudely, referring to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company as thieves and robbers. After speaking in French, fearing that I did not understand, he repeated it in Shanghai dialect. I immediately refuted him, saying that offering a price for a sale, how could there be such absurd arguments? The church is asking for 390,000 taels, without any concessions, is it possible to force a sale? Is a counteroffer robbery? Moreover, the father should abide by Catholic rules, how can he arbitrarily scold people? The matter concerns public insult. How should this be handled? I await your instructions. As for the Father of the Sande Church, who previously sent a letter willing to sell the land, and now, upon a counteroffer, immediately withdraws it completely, it is very close to child's play, disregarding Sino-French relations, and clearly failing to live up to the French Consul General's hard work in mediating this case. Our side seems to be unable to allow this lightly. I hereby state this. Respectfully addressed to Commissioner Li of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. Attorney Kao Shuo, Seal, March 21st.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Reply to the Sande Church: Respectfully replying to the letter from attorney Bahe on March 18th, representing your church, regarding your church's previous letter on November 3, 1930, agreeing to sell the Gold Profit Source pier at Registered Love No. 69 to our company, because the counteroffer differs from the price requested, it is considered difficult to approach the matter, there is no need to continue negotiations, and it will be unconditionally withdrawn, please inform, etc. After investigation, the pier on this land was originally built by our company with huge sums of money, and later ceded to your church. The deed states that it must be leased to our company for use and cannot be leased to others. The details of the negotiations between the Prime Minister's Office of the previous Qing Dynasty and the Shanghai Daotai with the French Minister and the French Consul General are all on file and can be easily reviewed. In this case, out of respect for Consul General Gan's hard work in mediation, your church formally agreed to sell, and both parties are negotiating, with various authorities in the French Concession mediating, hoping to achieve a satisfactory result. Unexpectedly, our company negotiated in good faith, but Father Hsia-ch'i, the manager of your church, acted arbitrarily and recklessly, arbitrarily slandering and even contradicting himself, which is very close to child's play. Our company believes that Father Hsia-ch'i's actions intentionally hinder the transportation of the National Government and will infringe upon the friendship between China and France. If your church does not realize the situation soon and follow a proper path, our company will have to take necessary measures. Any other unexpected events that occur as a result, the responsibility will be fully borne by your church. I hereby send this letter to your church for investigation. March 24th.

Commemorating the Brave, Great, and Heroic "March 29th" 77

A. Our Necessary Understanding: (1) The glorious Republic of China is the price paid with the blood and heads of revolutionary martyrs. (2) The spirit of the martyrs who sacrificed for the revolution is truly earth-shattering and can arouse the weak and make ghosts and gods weep. (3) Because of the continuous self-sacrifice and willingness to die for righteousness of the revolutionary martyrs, the revolutionary trend of thought has permeated the land and cannot be stopped once it starts. (4) The martyrdom of the revolutionary martyrs is not only a great loss to our party, but also the most serious loss to the Republic of China. (5) The revolutionary spirit of the martyrs will be like the sun and moon traversing the sky, the rivers flowing on the earth, and will be immortalized in the history of the Republic of China.

B. Our Necessary Efforts: (1) Strive to increase knowledge, supplement experience, cultivate personality, and strengthen physique, to serve the party and the country. (2) Emulate the fighting spirit and courage of sacrifice of the martyrs, and engage in revolutionary construction. (3) Inherit the legacy of the martyrs, strive for the abolition of all unequal treaties, complete a truly independent and free country, and achieve the goal of government of the people, by the people, and for the people.

Propaganda Department of the Shanghai Special City Executive Committee of the Chinese Nationalist Party

Various Industry Groups Discussed Unifying Weights and Measures Yesterday 78

Six Measures Decided

To Be Implemented on July 1st

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, under the order of the Bureau of Social Affairs, convened representatives from various industry groups to discuss the unification of weights and measures. The details of yesterday's meeting are recorded below:

Representatives Present: Silk Factory Industry Wang Xiaolai, Southern Goods Industry Zheng Chengqing, New Medicine Industry Sun Choucheng, Flour Factory Gu Xinyi, Cotton Cloth Industry Chen Songyuan, Egg Factory Industry Cui Jinggong, Clothing Industry Wu Zhihao, Fresh Meat Association Shen Xie, Fur Industry Jiang Zhigang, and more than 60 others. Wang Xiaolai was elected as chairman.

Chairman's Report: The chairman first gave a report, roughly stating: Today's meeting is based on the instructions of the Bureau of Social Affairs to discuss the matter of unifying weights and measures. Its meaning is like the three slogans in our country's commercial customs: fair transactions, no deception of the elderly or children, and unified and unwavering. But how can this be achieved? There must be a unified standard. In the past, our country's weights and measures were very uneven. Scales had sixteen ounces, ten ounces, and eight ounces. Rulers had sea rulers and Suzhou rulers. If they are not unified, not only will disputes often occur, but morally it is also very incompatible. Therefore, unifying the national weights and measures system has become an urgent matter, and the goal is to make the country consistent and in line with the international metric system.

Representatives' Speeches: Wu Huanru, the representative of the Bureau of Social Affairs, said: In the past, under the old system, weights and measures often caused disputes, and the people felt it was very difficult. In recent years, the government has been seeking to unify weights and measures, researching and improving methods, and establishing municipal weights and measures based on the international metric system to facilitate the promotion of the whole country. The city has established a weights and measures verification office, which is now equipped. It will register stores in the city that manufacture weights and measures and instruct them to manufacture new instruments in the future to achieve unification. Now, if representatives of various industry associations have any insightful opinions, please express them fully for discussion.

Verification Report: Zhou Zanming, the representative of the Shanghai Weights and Measures Verification Office, reported that the current unification of the weights and measures system is being handled by the National Weights and Measures Bureau urging various provinces and cities. The provincial government is responsible for the construction department, and the municipal government is responsible for the social affairs bureau. The implementation method of the Weights and Measures Verification Office is divided into five points: (1) Investigate the usage habits of various industries. (2) Promote the use of new instruments. (3) Verify the weights and measures of manufacturers and sellers. (4) Inspect the weights and measures already used by various industries. (5) Guide the use of new instruments. (6) Prohibit the use of old instruments.

Measures Decided: After discussion by the representatives, the following measures were decided: (1) July 1st was decided as the date for promoting the new system in the city. (Before the deadline for unification in the city) On the one hand, notify the members of each industry. On the other hand, register with the verification office. (2) Notify each industry to report the types and quantities of new instruments needed. (3) The verification office, based on the reports of various industries, urges the manufacturing factories to manufacture as much as possible to meet the needs. (4) Compare the new and old instruments, revise the prices, and compile simple conversion tables for distribution to various industries. (5) Assist the verification office in carrying out inspection affairs. (6) Execute other matters concerning the unification of weights and measures assigned by the Bureau of Social Affairs or the verification office.

Ministry of Finance Explains Key Points of Collecting Business Tax 87

Divides the Boundaries of Exemption from Business Tax

Specifies the Affixing of Stamps to Business Licenses

In order to promote business tax and prevent various disputes from arising during implementation, the Ministry of Finance specially telegraphed chambers of commerce in various provinces and cities yesterday to explain everything. The telegram is recorded below: For the matter of consultation and implementation: An investigation found that the provinces and cities are implementing the abolition of Likin, and are holding business tax to compensate for the case. The ministry has reported to the executive yuan to approve the general outline of business tax collection and supplementary measures and ordered the provinces and cities to comply with it. However, article 1 of the business tax general outline stipulates that companies that have paid income tax to the central government and those that have been collected special surtaxes by the central government are excluded. Article 1 of the supplementary measures stipulates that all banks, special companies, and tobacco and alcohol industries that have been levied license taxes are excluded. In addition, how much stamp duty should be affixed to business licenses used for business tax is also not provided in previous regulations. All of these should be clarified so that both tax collectors and taxpayers can follow the rules. The five explanation measures are listed below: (1) Factories or companies that have paid unified tax or special consumption tax shall not be levied business tax by the provinces, but merchants and stores selling and selling them shall still be levied business tax. (2) Provinces shall not levy business tax on those who specialize in the salt industry and have been levied salt tax by the central government, but stores selling miscellaneous goods that also operate retail salt shall still be levied business tax. (3) Provinces shall not levy business tax on those who specialize in the tobacco and alcohol industry and have been levied tobacco and alcohol license fees by the central government, but stores selling goods that also sell tobacco and alcohol shall still be levied business tax. (4) Stamp tax tickets shall be affixed to business licenses. Those with capital above 500 yuan shall affix 5 jiao per certificate, and those with capital below 500 yuan shall affix 1 jiao per certificate. (5) The central government shall levy exchange tax on exchanges, and the provinces shall not levy business tax. In addition to consulting, the above measures should be consulted for reference.

Minhang Chamber of Commerce Appeals for Correction of Business Tax 89

The Minhang Chamber of Commerce in Shanghai County submitted a document to the Ministry of Finance yesterday regarding business tax, requesting corrections. The abstract of the original presentation is recorded below: The presentation is to appeal for the correction of the regulations on business tax collection in Jiangsu and its implementation details, which exceed the outline, in order to conform to the precedent and alleviate merchants' difficulties. We believe that our country's industry and commerce have suffered from the harsh demands of Likin, and they have felt pain for more than 80 years. The central government, realizing the people's sentiments, resolutely decided to implement the abolition of Likin throughout the country on the 20th of this year. Hundreds of millions of people feel this virtue together. After the Likin is abolished, the income of the localities has suddenly decreased, and the budget is acutely insufficient. The provinces have held business tax to compensate for this. However, we believe that the abolition of Likin originally intended to eliminate bad policies and renew the people. The quality of the new tax system is of great importance to the interests of merchants and people. At the beginning of this founding, we must not ignore it. Therefore, we will present several points of disagreement between the business tax regulations of Jiangsu Province and its implementation details and the Ministry's regulations to our Minister for consideration: (1) The tax rate should be revised. (2) The taxation of goods should be changed. (3) Goods that have paid central taxes should be excluded. (4) Grains and firewood should be exempt from tax. (5) The method of collection should be as convenient as possible. (6) The bonus for the fine of 50% should be considered. (7) The business tax of the brokerage industry should be expressly exempted. The above seven items are only a few of the major ones. They are all related to the skin pain of merchants. Likin harms merchants, but there is still a day of abolition. Once the business tax regulations are approved and filed, there is no hope of cancellation. At the beginning of the creation, if the planning is slightly careless, the future of industry and commerce will be greatly affected.

China Aviation Corporation Investigates National Aviation Talent 91

The company held a board meeting yesterday.

The China Aviation Corporation held a board meeting the day before yesterday (the 24th) at the residence of Liu Shufan, the Director-General of the Postal Savings and Remittances Bureau. A total of six Chinese and American directors attended. The main points discussed were: (1) Actively

Page 10

deploying airports along the Beijing-Ping, Wuhan-Yichang lines to facilitate air navigation; (2) Recent assignment of American personnel: (A) Bender was appointed as Vice Chairman; (B) Hamilton and Saez were appointed as Directors; (C) Smith was appointed as Inspector; (3) Investigating aviation talent nationwide. The last question was discussed for a long time during the meeting. According to He Jiwu, the General Manager of the company, speaking to a reporter from the Guowen News Agency yesterday, China's aviation industry is booming, and the development of air transport is of great importance to the future of domestic transportation. Recruiting specialists is particularly important. Taking the company as an example, it currently employs six American pilots and ten Chinese pilots. This is sufficient for the time being, but after the Beijing-Ping, Wuhan-Yichang lines start formally carrying passengers, and the Shanghai-Guangdong line, which is currently being planned, will also start soon, the need for talent is very high. The Northeast, and provinces such as Pingjin, Hasui, Min, Guang, and Gui are not lacking in aviation talent, but our country has never had a detailed investigation and statistics, resulting in talent being buried and unheard of. When the aviation industry needs pilots, it often spends huge salaries to hire foreigners. Currently, the Chinese and American directors of the company all agree to search for Chinese aviation talent, and have entrusted aviation offices in various cities to conduct investigations, expecting to review and employ them when expanding in the future. The company's investigation letter to aviation offices in various cities is recorded below: Respectfully, although the development of our country's aviation industry has been temporary, the progress is truly surprising. It is a pity that new talent is often used by other states. This is due to the lack of domestic talent, but also because the usual inquiries are not thorough, and communication is rare, leading to this. In view of this, our office intends to conduct a large-scale investigation, collecting information on the origins, ages, experiences, etc., of all domestic aviation specialists, so as to facilitate communication and contact, which will be of some benefit to the future of domestic aviation. We have long admired your office for having established regulations for the aviation industry and understanding aviation talent like the back of your hand. We intend to attach a form with this letter, and hope that you will conduct a detailed investigation within your jurisdiction and show it to us for reference, in the spirit of public service. Sincerely, to: Aviation offices in Nanjing, Chongqing, Kunming, Changsha, Guangzhou, Taiyuan, Shenyang, etc.

Shanghai Banking Association Held General Meeting Yesterday 92

All members must submit opinions on the Banking Law by the deadline.

The Shanghai Banking Association held a general meeting at its clubhouse at No. 4 Hong Kong Road at 2:00 PM yesterday. All 24 members attended. After the meeting began, the following were discussed: (1) Members will submit their written opinions on the newly revised Banking Law of the Legislative Yuan within three days, which will be collected by the Banking Association and forwarded to the central government. Increase in Third-Class Passenger Tickets on Two Railways Difficult to Change 93

Ministry of Railways replies to letter from Municipal Chamber of Commerce

The Ministry of Railways replied to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday regarding the request to exempt the increase in third-class passenger tickets on the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo railways, stating that it was difficult to make a sudden change. The original letter stated, "Regarding your association's telegram on behalf of Xiantai, regarding the increase in freight rates on the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo railways, please allow the exemption of the increase in the price of third-class passenger tickets to benefit the common people, etc., which shows your concern for railway administration and consideration for people's livelihoods. However, it is found that the current price of gold is expensive, and not only the railway suffers huge losses, but also all businesses are affected equally. Your association should be able to understand this situation, without the need for detailed explanation. This increase in freight rates on the two railways is actually to make up for business losses, which is a last resort. Moreover, the transportation surcharges on the two railways have also been limited by the Ministry, and the price increase for third-class passenger tickets is very small. After the increase, it is still low compared to other railways. During the period of railway financial difficulties, it is still a consideration for people's livelihoods in making up for losses. Now that the case has been implemented, it is even more difficult to make a sudden change. Approved as before, reply accordingly, and hope to follow the original instructions," etc.

Social Bureau Mediates the Sale of Sanxin Yarn Factory 95

Summoned for questioning this afternoon

Labor representatives put forward conditions yesterday

After the Sanxin Yarn Factory on Yangshupu Road announced its sale, the Ministry of Industry and the Municipal Government ordered the Municipal Social Bureau to investigate and handle the matter. Yesterday, the bureau issued a notice to the labor representatives and Rong Zongjing, and scheduled a questioning session first for this afternoon to facilitate mediation. The situation obtained yesterday is recorded separately as follows:

Authorities mediate After receiving the news of the sale of the Sanxin Yarn Factory, the Municipal Social Bureau, because it is greatly related to the future of the Chinese textile industry, and it is necessary to pay attention to who it is sold to, sent staff to investigate thoroughly. Later, they received instructions from the Municipal Government and telegrams from the Ministry of Industry, all ordering investigation and handling, and the labor representatives repeatedly petitioned for relief. Therefore, Xu Zhi, a staff member of the Third Section, was designated to summon the cotton textile industry union of the Third Special Zone, Sheng Zecheng, the owner of the Sanxin Yarn Factory, and Rong Zongjing, the buyer of the machinery factory, for questioning at 1:00 PM today, in order to start mediation. The notices have been issued separately yesterday.

Notice to the union Yesterday, the Municipal Social Bureau, due to being ordered to handle the sale of the Sanxin Yarn Factory, issued a notice to the cotton textile industry union of the Third Special Zone, instructing all workers to wait for mediation. The petition was submitted, stating that the Sanxin Yarn Factory was being sold, requesting that severance pay be issued to maintain livelihood, etc. All were aware. Respectfully, immediately instruct them to wait for mediation, and do not obstruct the old and new reception, causing disputes. This is an important notice.

Order to Rong Zongjing Yesterday, the Social Bureau issued an order to Rong Zongjing, the general manager of Shenxin Yarn Factory, the buyer of the machinery of the Sanxin Yarn Factory, stating, "To order compliance, the Municipal Government issued Order No. 7683, based on the petition submitted by the cotton textile industry union of the Third Special Zone, stating that the Sanxin Yarn Factory was being sold, requesting that relief be provided and that remuneration be issued, etc. The deputy petition was forwarded, ordering immediate investigation and handling, and reporting, etc. Upon receiving this, while the investigation and handling were underway, a telegram from the Ministry of Industry was received, ordering immediate investigation and handling of the case. It was found that the factory had been established for a long time, and the employees had served for several years, or even dozens of years. Once the factory foundation is sold, the foundation is shaken, and the public is panicked. It is a matter of course. In addition to persuading the factory employees not to obstruct the old and new reception, and ordering them to wait for mediation, the reason for the order is that, in addition to submitting separate reports and instructions to the union, it is necessary to order compliance. This order."

Workers' conditions Yesterday, the cotton textile industry union of the Third Special Zone held a temporary meeting and put forward three requirements, and submitted them to the Social Bureau for review and handling. It was submitted, stating that the Sanxin Yarn Factory disregarded the livelihoods of the workers and rashly closed down and sold the factory. Now the conditions are put forward, and submitted to your bureau. It is requested that the factory owner, Sheng Zecheng, be ordered to fulfill the requirements as soon as possible, so as to comply with government laws and protect the survival of workers. This is a great benefit. Sincerely submitted. The three conditions are as follows: (A) Regarding the workers, a total of 3,716 people: (1) Severance pay: The average monthly salary of each person is 3.5 yuan, with a maximum of 18 yuan and a minimum of 9 yuan. The total salary for all workers for one month is 50,166 yuan. The severance pay should be for four months, totaling 200,664 yuan. (2) Living expenses: Workers aged 50 and above will be given 18 months of living expenses, and those under 50 will be given 6 months of living expenses. (B) Regarding the shift mechanics, oilers, and chief and deputy female supervisors, a total of 655 people: The average monthly salary of each person is 22.5 yuan, with a maximum of 30 yuan and a minimum of 15 yuan. The total for one month is 14,737.5 yuan. The severance pay and living expenses should be handled in the same way as the workers. (C) Regarding the Tongshan Hall, all the property of the Sanxin Factory Tongshan Hall should be handled by the employees themselves.

The Two Railway Unions in the Midst of Reorganization 98

The Union Reorganization Committee issued a letter to members

The reorganization committee of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Unions, having received repeated orders from the central government that the railway is an industrial union and can only establish one complete union, and cannot divide it into car service, machinery, or other names, decided after 64 reorganization committee meetings to reorganize all existing unions into branch offices. After the reorganization is completed, the council members of the two railway unions will be elected by the representative assembly. Yesterday, Zou Keqin, the director of the guidance section, summoned the representatives of various unions for talks and published the "Letter to All Members of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Unions on Reorganizing the Unions" to explain. The recording is as follows: "Fellow workers of the two railways, the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Unions are now starting to reorganize. Before the reorganization, the reasons for the reorganization should be explained to all workers, so as to avoid doubts and misunderstandings. For the sake of clarity, it is stated segment by segment as follows: (1) The general situation of the organization of the two railway unions in the past. In the past, worker groups were organized according to the organizational system set by the former Central People's Training Committee. In the vertical aspect, each union was established, and then the general union was produced. Not only were the two railways like this, but most other places were the same. Later, the central government abolished this organizational system, and the Union Law and the Union Law Enforcement Law were promulgated by the National Government one after another. Originally, they could be reorganized from scratch according to the laws and regulations, but because of the long-standing habits and too many doubts in the Union Law, looking around the country, the worker groups were still proceeding in the original way, and on the one hand, they were still hoping for the promulgation of the special trade union law, and the superiors never had specific methods to instruct. At this time of wandering and crossroads, at a loss, the association can only do its duty to actively reorganize the various unions of the two railways. At the same time, it also feels that the organization of the union is no different from the organization of the party department. They are all from the bottom up. No matter how the name changes in the future, the basic organization must first seek to be sound. Fortunately, we did this and got the unity of the workers of different professions in various parts. Now, there are more than ten individual organizations of the union that have been established one after another, and there are still several in the preparatory period. The general situation of the organization of the two railway unions in the past is roughly like this. (2) The basis for the reorganization. Article 6 of the Union Law states that only one union can be established for workers in the same industry or workers in the same occupation in the same area. Article 2 of the Union Law Enforcement Law states that an organization that gathers workers of different occupations in the same enterprise is an industrial union, and an organization that gathers workers of the same occupation is an occupational union. The central government stipulates that the railway union is an industrial union, and the railway area is the scope from the beginning to the end of the line. There is no doubt in law that the two railways can establish one union. However, the already established unions have different duties and different systems. Mixed organizations are not only difficult in fact, but also may cause disputes. These difficulties are felt by comrades who guide the organization of railway unions. Recently, the central government also knows this actual situation and must find a way to remedy it. Therefore, it issued a simplified organizational rule for the branch offices of the railway union, but at the same time, it does not allow the various unions under the same enterprise to stand side by side, and must be reorganized according to law. We have this concrete plan, and all kinds of psychology that were formerly depressed and doubtful are gone. At the meeting of the reorganization committee, the plan to reorganize the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Unions was passed. (3) The significance of the reorganization. Workers join the union because the union can protect workers and seek benefits for workers. The reason why the union has this power is because it has the qualifications of a legal person. If it is not organized according to the laws and regulations of the union, the party department will of course stop it, and the government will not be able to guarantee it. Then, where can we get the qualifications of a legal person? The significance of reorganizing the union is to make the union legal, and to enable the legal union to protect workers and seek benefits for workers. Moreover, the reorganization does not have much change, but the names of the staff are different. The original organization is still preserved, and the original system is still maintained, so that the former scattered state of each separate state becomes a whole united "Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Unions" to maximize the obligations assumed by the union. (4) How to reorganize and the procedure of reorganization. The reorganization does not have much change. It has been said above that the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway should establish a union. Under the union, branch offices are established separately. The reorganization procedure is to first establish the various branch offices, and then elect representatives to produce directors and supervisors to formally establish the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Unions. At this time, all the procedures are completed. The highest party department certifies it and registers with the highest competent authority. Fellow workers, we need the whole union, especially the legal union. At the time of this reorganization, I hope everyone will work together and support it together," etc., etc.

Jardine Matheson Denies Compensation for Goods in Changsha 100

Changsha Chamber of Commerce representatives continue to negotiate

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce previously requested the Jardine Matheson to compensate the Changsha Chamber of Commerce. When the Red Army captured Changsha, the ship company was unable to handle it and the goods stored in the warehouse were all looted. It is now known that the company has replied to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, stating, "Respectfully received the great letter. During the Communist Party's looting of Changsha in July last year, our company deeply regretted it. The looting of our company's Changsha warehouse, in fact, maintaining local order is the responsibility of the authorities. Before the arrival of the Red Army, there was early warning. Changsha merchants should have tried their best to take appropriate measures to protect their goods before the army withdrew. At that time, the situation was serious, and it was difficult for merchants to leave Changsha. Moreover, it was found in our company's books that some consignees had taken the goods away before the provincial capital was looted. Then, the Changsha merchants at that time already knew that the local turmoil was enough to endanger their goods. The responsibility that the merchants should bear should be recognized by everyone. Moreover, everything has been stipulated in our company's bill of lading terms. Our company's warehouse was unfortunately the first to be looted. The warehouses near Zou, which belong to other shipping companies, would have been unavoidable if foreign gunboats had not come out and interfered. Our company, as a shipping company, cannot protect the warehouse in the midst of turmoil. As for the authorities responsible for public security, they have stopped exercising their powers. Therefore, our company cannot be responsible for the losses that occurred at this time." It is heard that the Municipal Chamber of Commerce has transferred the letter to the Changsha Chamber of Commerce for reference. At the same time, representatives of the Changsha Chamber of Commerce have personally gone to the company to negotiate on the basis of reason.

Chen Gengxin Kidnapped 111

Four Thugs in Total

Acted on Ningbo Road

Thugs Informed the Victim

About the Car's Whereabouts

Around 7 o'clock last night, Chen Gengxin, a major yarn merchant, was kidnapped by thugs in front of a friend's door at 68 Ningbo Road in the French Concession. The details are recorded as follows:

Chen Shihao Outwardly Strong, Inwardly Weak: Chen Shihao, styled Gengxin, is 51 years old, from Dinghai, Ningbo. He is the comprador of the Baoxing Yarn Factory in Dachang, Zhabei. The factory's main wholesale office is located at 243 Ningbo Road, Wufu Lane, in the Public Concession. His family resides at 870 Hengqing Lane, Lloyd Road. He has two sons and one daughter. The eldest son works at the factory's wholesale office, and the younger son is still studying. Recently, due to the poor business of the yarn factory, the factory could not escape unscathed, so Chen only holds an empty title and is outwardly strong but inwardly weak.

Visiting Mr. Li Every Afternoon: Chen met a friend named Li Chijie about a year ago. Li is in his thirties and used to work at the Bank of Communications but has been unemployed for a long time. He keeps a prostitute and resides on the third floor of the Jin Yu Law Firm at 68 Ningbo Road in the French Concession. Chen takes a car to Li's place every day around 3 pm. It has become a daily routine, regardless of the weather, and Li and the prostitute treat him with respect, regarding him as an honored guest.

Meeting Yarn Merchant, Visiting Li Earlier: Yesterday morning around 9 am, Li Chijie went to the wholesale office to negotiate with Chen because a yarn merchant from Changshu wanted to trade with the Baoxing factory, and Li acted as a broker. Before leaving, he asked Li to meet him earlier. At 3:30 pm, Chen took the green car No. 3715 directly to Li's place.

Four Thugs Carried Out the Kidnapping: Chen was at Li's place, and before he knew it, the clock struck seven. Chen bid farewell. Just as he stepped into the car, as the chauffeur Peng Amao (from Tongzhou) was starting the engine, four thugs suddenly rushed out from the roadside, each holding a handgun. They forbade the chauffeur from making any noise, then rushed into the car and forced the chauffeur to drive west. At that time, Ningbo Road was lined with vendors and crowded with tourists, and no one noticed. Even his friends Li and the prostitute were completely unaware.

Thugs Notified the Location of the Car: The car went past North Chu Chia Chiao, went straight to the west along Avenue Joffre, and soon turned into Hualong Road. The thugs pushed the chauffeur Peng Amao down. One thug drove the car to the north and disappeared. After Peng was driven away, he planned to return to the Avenue Paul Beau report to Chen's younger brother Hansan. But before the chauffeur arrived, the telephone at Chen's home suddenly rang. He listened carefully and heard the thugs informing that the car was abandoned near the dog racing field on Avenue du Père Robert, and told him to send someone to pick it up immediately. At the same time, the chauffeur Peng Amao arrived, and then he knew that Chen had been kidnapped. When Chen's younger brother heard the news, he was terrified and rushed to Li's house at 68 Ningbo Road to inquire. Unexpectedly, Li was still as if in a dream. They went to Chen's house together on Lloyd Road to inform the family, and they sent someone to drive the car back while deliberating on how to deal with the aftermath.

Public Entertainment Venues Without Permits 113

The Municipal Public Security Bureau stipulates three measures

The Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau issued an order to the district heads, stating, "For the purpose of issuing a notification, regarding the case reported by Zhou Pu, the fourth district head, to investigate and handle public entertainment venues without permits, we have already ordered an investigation. It is found that there are nine entertainment venues in the jurisdiction, none of which have permits. The former district head only ordered them to submit application forms and did not punish or stop their business. Please instruct us on how to handle this situation." Based on this, we find that this notice orders each district to investigate public entertainment venues. If there are those who have not been permitted by the bureau and given a permit, they should be punished and their business should be stopped. They should still be ordered to fill out an application form and apply for a permit. This refers to those who specialize in public entertainment venues. As for tea houses with storytelling or local opera venues, and other entertainment venues, most of them have tea house registration certificates from the bureau, which is different from operators who specialize in entertainment venues. If they are all punished and ordered to close down due to not having permits, then seven or eight out of ten of these tea houses with incidental entertainment venues, a large number, would be affected. Once they are closed, it would take time to apply for a permit, which would be related to the livelihood of merchants and the monthly donations of the Finance Bureau. According to the reports from each district, the handling of tea houses with entertainment venues that do not have permits, whether punished or not, is not consistent. This is not only the case in the fourth district. It is urgent to distinguish the situations, stipulate measures, and issue a notice to comply with them to ensure uniformity and fairness. The following measures are hereby stipulated: (1) Before the promulgation of the Shanghai Municipal Public Entertainment Venue Management Regulations in October 19th year of the Republic of China (1930), all old tea houses with storytelling, local opera, or other entertainment venues that have tea house registrations from the bureau are different from private setups and should be exempt from punishment and a deadline for closure. They should be limited to filling out an application form and sending it to the district offices for submission to the bureau for verification and handling. (2) Tea houses with entertainment venues, as well as specialized theaters, cinemas, storytelling venues, local opera venues, and other public entertainment venues, even if they were established before the promulgation of the Public Entertainment Venue Management Regulations in October 19th year of the Republic of China, but the tea houses do not have registration certificates and the entertainment venues do not have permits, are considered violations. They should be punished in accordance with Article 33, Section 1 of the Violation of Police Regulations for illegal operation. Since they have been operating for years and have donation permits from the Finance Bureau, they are temporarily exempt from closure and are still given a deadline to fill out an application form and send it to the district offices for submission to the bureau for verification and handling. (3) After the promulgation of the Public Entertainment Venue Management Regulations, new tea houses with entertainment venues and all kinds of specialized public entertainment venues that have not been registered and permitted by the bureau are considered deliberate violations of regulations and should be punished according to the law and their business should be stopped. After filling out an application form and submitting it to the bureau, they will be verified and handled. The above three measures, in addition to being distributed separately, are hereby ordered to the district head to immediately comply with and implement them diligently and report back. This order is issued on March 21st, 20th year of the Republic of China. Director Chen Xizeng."

Extorting Money from Criminals' Families

Selling Their Wives If They Don't Have Money

If Public Officials Are Like This

Where Is the Discipline of the Country

First Arresting Jiang Zhenggen: Wang Yaowu, the captain of the Yixing County Public Security Bureau police team, arrested Jiang Zhenggen (also known as Wang Tinghai) because he committed a robbery in Yixing. After being strictly pursued by the local government, he fled to Shanghai. Therefore, he joined forces with the Huike patrolman to detain Jiang and escort him to the Special District Local Court. Because Captain Wang did not provide a transfer document, it was not convenient to hand over the prisoner and take him away for trial. It was ordered that Jiang be detained temporarily, pending a letter from the Yixing County Government for further verification. Wang returned to Yixing to report, and the county magistrate gave him an official document, and he came to Shanghai again.

Subsequently Capturing Wang Ronghai: Unexpectedly, upon arriving in Shanghai, he also captured Wang Ronghai and sent him to the Huike patrolman. According to Captain Wang, Ronghai was Zhenggen's accomplice, and the patrol head detained him. The next morning, he and Zhenggen were escorted to the Special Court. Wang then submitted an official document requesting extradition. However, Ronghai was captured by Wang on his second trip to Shanghai, so the official document from Yixing County only had Zhenggen's name, so it was still not possible to take both of them away.

Captain Wang Extorted Money: Moreover, during the interrogation, both of them denied being robbers, and Zhenggen even claimed that since Ronghai was also detained, he heard Ronghai say in the detention center that Captain Wang had extorted 200 yuan from his family, promising to release him after receiving the money. His family was poor, and Captain Wang had actually kidnapped his wife and sold her in Shanghai, causing them to be separated. He cried bitterly, banging his head against the wooden wall he was leaning against.

Two More Arrested: According to the confession, the judge questioned Ronghai, who confessed that Captain Wang had indeed sold Jiang's wife. Judge Xu also questioned them briefly because he had not submitted a formal transfer document, and ordered Pan and Xu to be detained pending a letter from Yixing for further interrogation.

Selling Hemp Skin: At this time, the Huike patrolman had verified Wang Yaowu's kidnapping of Jiang's wife and had also learned that Pan and Xu were both Wang Yaowu's followers. Before Xu was arrested, he was specially ordered by his master to kidnap Jiang's wife to Shanghai with Li Awu and take her to 295 Xizang Road to entrust her to a hemp skin dealer, setting a price of 250 yuan, with 200 yuan paid to Yaowu and the remaining 50 yuan going to Awu.

Ending Up as a Beggar: The hemp skin dealer saw that Jiang's wife was not young and not attractive, and the asking price was unusually high, so it was difficult for him. Because of the friendship, he could not refuse at the time, so he solicited around for three days, but no one was interested. He wanted to send her back, but Li and others did not want to raise this ugly woman. The hemp skin dealer also refused to provide long-term meals, so he issued an eviction order. Jiang's wife was a stranger in a foreign land and became a beggar, sleeping in the open and eating in the wind, not just for a day. The Patrolman's Accusation: The other day, she was begging along the door on Lloyd Road when she suddenly met a detective who was ordered to investigate. The detective learned the whole story and took the woman back to the Huike patrolman. He then investigated Li and others and arrested Awu in Zhabei and sent him to the police station in charge. Subsequently, his accomplice Zhou Cairong was arrested. However, the hemp skin dealer's whereabouts are still unknown. Questioning Captain Wang: The police captain Wang Yaowu was also summoned to the case. After Judge Ge Zhiqin interrogated him, he ordered all the defendants to be remanded in custody pending the transfer of Li Awu from the Municipal Public Security Bureau for further interrogation, and ordered the investigating detectives to also take Wang Yaowu to the patrolman to inquire about everything in order to clarify the truth.

Suspicious Case of Corpse in a Box 117

White-haired Men and Women

Decomposed Bodies Divided into Two Sections

Two small wooden boxes were suddenly found on the open space opposite the Jiangxi Guild Hall on South Railway Station Branch Road yesterday morning, each containing a corpse, which had decomposed, but the hair was still there, white hair, seemingly male and female. The most strange thing is that both corpses were cut into two sections, and two small wooden boxes were placed on top, inside which were dry bones. Nearby residents gathered to discuss, saying that it was a case of a corpse in a box for the purpose of murder, and those who went to watch were endless. However, looking closely, it seems that the two corpses must have been corpses in intact coffins. The rogue stole a good coffin, and then placed it in a wooden box, so he cut the corpse into two sections. If it was murder, it would not have decomposed so that the face was difficult to recognize. Since it was not reported to the court for inspection, it is still difficult to clarify the truth.

Passers-by Urinated in a Small Alley

Factory Owner Fired Two Shots After Hearing the News

He employed more than a hundred workers and the business was booming. Ma Haiwen from Hunan was originally a peddler. Due to a sudden need to urinate, he ran into a small alley on the side of the factory. Chang Huinan, the factory's accountant from Anhui, saw him and, because it was not a place for urination, ordered Ma to drive him away. When Ma entered the alley, the passerby had already gone far away. Chang Huinan then suspected that Ma had deliberately delayed, so he could not reprimand the urinator. He arbitrarily scolded Ma, and they started arguing with each other. Zhang Tiankai happened to arrive at the factory, and Chang told Zhang about it. Zhang was furious and spoke sternly to Ma. Ma was also unwilling to back down, so they wrestled each other. Zhang had a handgun that he carried with him. At this time, he suddenly used this thing, holding the gun and shooting, firing twice in a row. Ma quickly avoided, without injury. Afterwards, Ma reported to the Jing'an Temple patrolman, who sent detectives to Zhang's residence at 109 Avenue de Conty, arrested Zhang, and searched out a handgun, three bullets, one bullet casing, and one bullet box. He was escorted to the Special District Local Court yesterday, and Judge Ge interrogated him. The patrolman's lawyer Zhang Tianyin claimed that it has not yet been decided whether the case should be prosecuted for the crime of interfering with freedom under Article 319 of the Criminal Code, or for the crime of attempted murder under Article 282, Section 2. He is now prosecuting it as a crime of interfering with freedom, and if it is deemed inappropriate after the interrogation, it should be corrected. He then recounted the circumstances of the incident. The defendant Zhang Tiankai hired Jiang Yiping and Zheng Wenkai as lawyers to defend him. Then, Ma Haiwen was summoned for questioning, who testified that Zhang first slapped him on the cheeks, then kicked him in the chest, and then fired a shot at him, the bullet flying past him. He was extremely frightened, so he hugged Mr. Chang tightly. He did not see clearly when the defendant fired the second shot. Finally, he was dragged into the factory and beaten. When questioned, the accused confessed that because he had received threatening letters, he had donated to the Public Works Department to obtain a handgun for self-defense. Last night, he entered the factory, heard a lot of noise, and saw people fighting, and the order was very chaotic. At first, he did not know the reason, and when he asked Chang Huinan, he learned that the matter started with Ma Haiwen. At that time, Ma rushed towards me with an iron rod, so I fired a shot at the ground as a warning, telling Ma to give up the iron rod. He refused and wanted to commit violence, so he fired the second shot, and Ma escaped. My firing was really for self-defense and had no ill intentions. The iron rod held by Ma has been sent to the patrolman this morning. Chinese and Western detectives immediately declared in court that they had not seen any iron rod sent to the patrolman and requested that the case be postponed for investigation. The defendant's lawyer then requested bail for the defendant. Judge Ge ordered Zhang Tiankai to post a security of 5,000 yuan and wait for a further hearing on the 30th of this month.

Murder of a Concubine - The Culprit Returned from the Capital to Shanghai 119

Allegedly, the Concubine Had Another Lover

Ma Songting, a native of Suqian, strangled his concubine, Song Qiaobao, a native of Suzhou, to death at 373 Hejian Road on the morning of February 13th last year, hid the body under the bed, stole the woman's private stash of a gold bracelet, four gold rings, and 150 yuan in cash, and fled without a trace. More than a year later, his brother, Ma Shouting, suddenly reported to the Yangshupu Police Station that his younger brother, Ma Songting, had been captured by the Nanjing Public Security Bureau. The police chief immediately requested the Special District Local Court to prepare a document and send Detective Shen Yuzhou to the capital to bring him back to Shanghai. Yesterday morning, Judge Feng opened the court for interrogation. Lawyer Li Zhishan of the police station stated that the defendant had confessed at the police station that he strangled the woman to death with a rope because she had another lover, but denied stealing any property. Ma Shouting then testified that in May of the year before last, his brother, along with the deceased and her mother, Song Gao, came to Shanghai from Suzhou and lived in the pavilion of his house. They had always been on good terms. On the day of the incident, at 10:00 AM, Song Gao suddenly went to the Third Factory of a Japanese company and told him that her daughter Qiaobao and Songting were both missing, along with some gold jewelry and money. He immediately took leave from the factory to help search for them. At 7:00 PM in the evening, he finally discovered Qiaobao's body under the bed, her neck strangled with a rope, and Songting was still missing. He suspected that he was the culprit and went to Suzhou and Kunshan to search for him, and recently learned that he had been arrested in Beijing. When questioned, Ma Songting claimed to be a dealer in old goods. That morning, he went to Yinxiang Port to collect old goods and returned home half an hour later. As soon as he entered the door, Song Gao shouted loudly, "Songting is back!" Qiaobao heard the sound and came downstairs and prevented him from going upstairs. Then he saw a man jump onto the roof and escape. He suspected that the man must be Qiaobao's lover. He scolded her, but Qiaobao slapped him and bit his arm,缠绕不停 (entangled him endlessly), so he strangled her to death with a麻 rope (flax rope) (or 麻绳, depending on typesetting in Chinese). He did not hide the body under the bed and fled immediately, and did not take any gold jewelry or silver dollars. The court ordered the defendant to be detained and adjourned the hearing for further investigation.

Huang Yutang Sentenced to Twelve Years of Imprisonment

The Remaining Eight Acquitted and Released

The Shanghai Municipal Council's Annual Report for Last Year 121

Released Yesterday

The Shanghai Municipal Council's report for 1930 was released yesterday. It includes:

The Commandant of the Shanghai Volunteer Corps reported that at the end of last year, the entire corps had 1,857 members, 93 fewer than at the end of the previous year. Most of the reduction was due to repeated violations of the regulations, resulting in forced discharge. The American Company performed the best among all units.

The Fire Brigade reported that there were 671 alarms within the settlement last year, 19 fewer than the previous year. However, the loss ratio increased from 0.094% to 0.148%. Property at risk totaled taels 71,204,021. Annual water consumption was 1,421,450 gallons, and the hoses used could stretch 42 miles. There were 17 deaths, compared to 45 last year. The brigade also assisted in extinguishing fires outside the settlement 25 times.

The Police Department reported that last year, there were 40 armed confrontations with bandits during arrests. Four Chinese officers were killed and 13 were injured. Fifteen bandits were killed and 14 were injured. At the end of last year, there was a shortage of 151 Chinese officers. Due to the limited space in the training center, it was impossible to train many people at the same time to quickly fill the vacancies. It is now planned to hire qualified Chinese personnel to serve as patrolmen, with the aim of assigning one Chinese patrolman to each police district to manage police affairs.

The Police Court Advocate reported that 97,665 cases were prosecuted in the Local Court last year, with 19,457 convictions.

The Public Works Department reported that construction within the settlement reached a new record last year. Based on the estimated value of the licenses issued, private construction costs amounted to taels 46,633,800. In addition, there were miscellaneous projects worth taels 2,000,000. Public construction was also substantial, totaling approximately taels 27,000,000 for the year. However, due to the fall in the price of silver and the rise in the cost of building materials compared to last year, it is estimated that approximately taels 10,000,000 was due to the increase in expense due to the high cost of gold and the low cost of silver, so the ratio of construction costs only increased by about 30% to 35% over last year. A total of 6,818 Chinese-style houses and city houses were added throughout the year. After deducting the 3,796 houses that were demolished, there was a net increase of 3,022 houses. 327 Western-style houses were added, but after deducting the 309 houses that were demolished, there was a net increase of only 18 houses. In addition, new and renovated buildings included 3 hotels, 5 Western-style apartments, 35 office buildings, 298 Western-style shops, 6 theaters, 6 schools, 3 cotton mills, 24 factories, 64 warehouses, 1 hospital, 3 telephone exchanges, and 1,002 other buildings.

Shanghai's All-Day Broadcasting Radio Station 123

Shanghai is a meeting place for Chinese and foreigners, and all kinds of businesses are thriving. However, a perfect and excellent broadcasting station is still lacking. It is now reported that the world-renowned Reuters News Agency and the well-reputed Meilingdeng Advertising Company in this city have jointly established a wireless broadcasting company with a Chinese and Western board of directors to oversee its operation. They have already built a broadcasting machine at 115 Edward Road in the Meilingdeng Building, which can reach a distance of 500 miles. A consulting group composed of wireless radio experts from various wireless radio companies in Shanghai, such as the United States Wireless Radio Company, Philips Trading Company, Telefunken Wireless Telegraph Wheeler Company, Asia Electric Company, and Cananda, will provide guidance to ensure that daily broadcasting is uninterrupted. Furthermore, there is a program committee dedicated to scheduling various interesting programs, which will be performed by members of the Shanghai ABC Drama Troupe. Mr. Gan Pu, the principal of the Huatong Public School, has also been invited to prepare for the transmission of English education, which is a good opportunity for Chinese people to practice English. The wireless radio management is under the direction of Mr. Auster, who has extensive experience in this field in the United States. Every day at 1:00 PM and 8:30 PM, Reuters news from abroad or about the Pacific region is broadcast in Chinese and Western languages. Chinese and foreign newspapers will also join in broadcasting local news, and Reuters' local financial news will be reported in Chinese. The broadcasting station aims to continuously broadcast various beneficial and interesting programs from 11:00 AM to 11:00 PM every day to serve the listeners. The station has been decorated by the Biju Company and has two broadcasting studios, a reception room, and an office. There are also two windows separated by glass so that the broadcasting situation can be observed from outside the room, which is particularly unique. Twelve musicians have been hired to be available for customers to choose from. Currently, each wireless radio company in Shanghai broadcasts various programs twice a week, which is very effective in terms of advertising. The equipment is now being installed, and broadcasting will begin in late April or early May. The Ministry of Communications has also issued a license. For more information, please contact Reuters News Agency and Meilingdeng Company.

The French Police Raid a Trafficking Organization and an Opium Den 126

French Police Detective Peng Shitian, Chinese Detective Chief Inspector Shen Defu, Inspector Chen Sanlin, Chief Detective Lu Jinchen, Deputy Detective Mao Jinsheng, and others discovered that Zhang Shixin, a native of Taizhou, had recently set up a private opium trafficking organization at No. 14, Jianli Lane, Zhengjia Muqiao Street, Dama Roadkou. Wang Zien also set up an opium den upstairs in the same house, allowing foreigners to eat opium inside, violating the ban. Therefore, they went there the night before last and seized 37 pounds of opium and three sets of opium smoking paraphernalia and lamps. They also arrested more than a dozen opium smokers and brought them all to the police station. The opium smokers were fined and released. Zhang and others were released on bail and sent to the French Court yesterday for investigation. First, the police chief reported the previous situation. When questioned, Zhang and Wang confessed to setting up a private opium trafficking organization and selling opium. The opium and opium smoking paraphernalia were confiscated.

Education News

Important News

Ministry of Education Proposes to the League of Nations 134

Exchange of University Professors

Yesterday, the Ministry of Education sent a letter to the League of Nations suggesting that Chinese universities exchange professors with European and American universities in order to promote academic communication and cooperation between China and the West. The letter was written in English, and the main points of the original letter are translated as follows: Sirs, Our Ministry has recently received a suggestion from the President of Nanjing Central University that, based on the cooperation between China and the League of Nations in other undertakings, in order to promote academic communication between Chinese universities and European universities, we propose that the League of Nations send renowned professors to China to hold lectures. If the League of Nations agrees to this, China is very willing to send renowned domestic scholars, such as writers, philosophers, historians, and antiquarians, to lecture abroad. At the same time, the League of Nations should also select renowned European and American university professors, such as medical scientists, natural scientists, and political and legal scholars, to lecture in China for the purpose of exchange. This method will undoubtedly promote Chinese and Western cultures and facilitate communication of ideas. In practical terms, Central University is very welcoming of the League of Nations sending professors to China to hold lectures. Furthermore, the university currently needs a professor of English literature (who must be British), a professor of geography who can specially emphasize field work, and a professor of geology who specializes in geological structure and knows how to conduct field geological surveys. The latter two are preferred to be of German, Austrian, Swedish, or Swiss nationality and proficient in teaching in English. If the League of Nations considers this method feasible, our Ministry hopes to first send the aforementioned professors to China to lecture. When necessary, China will also send renowned scholars to lecture in Europe. As for the monthly salary for these exchange lectures, Central University can only offer 320 yuan in national currency. Our Ministry hopes for an possible indication of this special cooperation. If necessary, we may seek financial assistance from other sources to subsidize the expenses of exchange lectures in China. Our Ministry is not very clear about the scope of the League's work in cultural movements. Therefore, we would like to receive detailed instructions on the possibility of China cooperating effectively with the League's organizations, especially the International Institute of Intellectual Cooperation and the Educational Activities Photography Institute. Our Ministry welcomes individual contact with the League's organizations. The first step towards this goal is to propose Mr. Wu Zhihui as a member of the League of Nations Committee on Intellectual Cooperation. Mr. Wu will personally attend the committee meeting in July this year, and his secretary can help with liaison and progress on this matter and other cooperative matters.

The Directors of the Education Bureaus of Jiangning and Jiangdu Represent 21 Counties in Jiangsu and Anhui to Petition the Ministry 137

Regarding the case of the education salt tax being assigned to the tax inspection office for collection, a special dispatch from Yangzhou stated that since the northward migration of salt transportation, all previous methods of paying taxes and levies have been gradually changed. It is now heard that the salt tax of 21 counties in Jiangsu and Anhui, including Jiangdu and Tianchang, has also been assigned to the Yangzhou tax inspection office for collection. This has caused panic among the education bureaus of the respective counties. It is recently heard that the directors of the education bureaus of the counties have jointly elected Tian Shunlin, the director of the Jiangning Education Bureau, and Chen Da, the director of the Jiangdu Education Bureau, to draft a document and personally go to the Ministry of Finance to petition. The original document is copied below to give a general idea of the past and present situation of the salt tax. The document states: "We have investigated that the education taxes of the 21 counties belonging to Jiangsu Province, including Jiangning and Jiangdu, as well as Jurong, Liuhe, Lishui, Gaochun, Jiangpu, Yizheng, Gaoyou, Baoying, Xinghua, Taixian, Dongtai, Rugao, Nantong, Haimen, Funing, Yangzhou, Yancheng, and Anhui Province's Tianchang, regarding the additional tax on salt, have always been collected by the Yangzhou Salt Transport Office under the Lianghuai salt tax item and allocated to the bureaus. This has been the case for many years. Recently, a letter from the office stated that on February 21 of this year, it received document No. 2255 from the Yangzhou Tax Inspection Office stating, 'Upon investigation, the additional tax on salt will be collected by this office from March 1 of this year and has been ordered to be notified accordingly. We have investigated that the Jiangdu County education fee of five cents per dan of Huainan salt is collected by the office and directly sent to the Yangzhou Educational Assets Office for verification and collection. Now, from March 1, it will be collected by this office and should be paid by the salt merchants along with the regular and additional taxes and verified and collected by the Bank of China in Yangzhou and credited to the account of the Ministry of Finance to comply with the original plan. In addition to separate instructions, we hereby instruct the office to immediately notify the salt merchants for their information.' Upon receiving this, Director Shunlin and Director Da consulted with the directors of the aforementioned 21 counties' education bureaus, who replied successively that the additional tax on salt is used to offset local education expenses and is very important. Once it is assigned to the tax inspection office for collection, they are sincerely afraid that the foundation will be shaken, which will affect education expenses. They also stated that it was reported that the 11th State Council meeting of the Executive Yuan resolved to inform the ministry to follow the instructions. Now that the Yangzhou Tax Inspection Office has already instructed the Salt Transport Office to collect the additional tax on salt from March 1, the education expenses of the 21 counties will not be allocated as usual from March. In this situation, it is necessary to jointly request the protection of the principle of independent education expenses. Therefore, they unanimously elected Director Shunlin and Director Da to go to the capital and provincial capital to petition separately. In addition to submitting a separate report to the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education and submitting it to the Jiangsu Provincial Government for consultation with the ministry, we humbly request the ministry to consider the importance of local education and earnestly request that the additional tax on salt be directly allocated under the Lianghuai salt tax item as before. We also request that the Bank of China in Yangzhou be allowed to retain it, and the Salt Transport Office will still be allowed to collect and distribute it on its behalf to maintain education and avoid complications. Is this appropriate? We humbly request your approval for compliance."

The First Enrollment of Subsidized Students by the Impoverished Education Fund Committee 140

The Qinghan (Impoverished) Education Fund, initiated by Mr. Wu Yun Chu of Tianchu Ajinomoto Factory, has finalized its regulations for the first enrollment of subsidized students. The enrollment notice will be published in newspapers shortly. The enrollment regulations are extracted as follows: (The Qinghan Education Fund Committee's Regulations for the First Enrollment of Subsidized Students) (1) This committee will provide scholarships to assist impoverished students in entering universities, offering twelve scholarships specifically for students studying chemistry and chemical engineering. However, the committee reserves the right to leave vacancies based on examination results. (2) The scholarship amount is set at 200 to 300 yuan in national currency per student per year. (3) Applicants must be graduates of public or registered private senior high schools. (4) Applicants must submit a formal application in the format prescribed by the committee, along with an investigation form, a guarantee letter, academic transcripts, and four 4-inch half-body photographs. These documents should be submitted by the school with an official letter of introduction to the committee by May 30th. (5) Applicants who pass the committee's initial review will be eligible to participate in the committee's formal examination, the date of which will be determined separately. (6) After being admitted by the committee, applicants should independently select and apply to universities in Zhejiang and Jiangsu provinces that offer science and engineering programs, subject to the committee's approval. Once admitted, they will be eligible for the scholarship. (7) Scholarship recipients should report their academic progress regularly. The committee reserves the right to suspend the scholarship if their conduct or grades are unsatisfactory. (8) Scholarship recipients should continue their studies until graduation. If they drop out midway, they must return the received funds to the committee. (9) Scholarship recipients have no obligation to repay the scholarship after graduation, but they are welcome to voluntarily donate to the committee's fund. (10) The rules for receiving the scholarship will be determined separately.
