The American Team Wins This Year's International Basketball Championship 151

Defeated China 38-27 in the third final last night

Alas, for the Chinese team in this year's International Basketball Tournament. After an initial disappointment, they defeated the strong American team in the second match, surviving by the skin of their teeth, and secured an equal opportunity in the third final at the Chinese Basketball Hall last night. Many people believed that the Chinese team would be able to defeat the Americans and retain the A.B.C. Cup for another year. However, things rarely go as planned, and in the final act, the Americans triumphed with a score of 38-27, snatching the championship trophy. The A.B.C. silver cup will once again be displayed by the American team for the first year.

Victory and defeat are inevitable

The American team's victory was due to their superior abilities and not a matter of luck. Squier, the outstanding player in the basketball world and the core of the American team, led the entire team to success with his skill and guidance. It can be said that he is a dragon among heroes, with exceptional intelligence and courage. Bissell and Mains, the cornerstones, played exceptionally well last night, scoring nearly half of the team's points. Pierce and Hannes did their best and could not be faulted. Only Smith was not at his usual level and was not as impressive as in the past.

Good and bad are publicly recognized

The Chinese team's performance was inconsistent. In the first ten minutes, they played with lightning speed and overwhelming force, surpassing the Americans in intensity. Lu Zhongsi was the mastermind, and the other four players were able to fully develop their skills. However, the good times did not last, and the situation gradually deteriorated. Despite regrouping and fighting hard, they were still lacking. The forwards lost their momentum, and the defenders made mistakes. In the end, they desperately tried to survive, but the overall situation was irreversible. Both sides then used their substitutes, which was a highlight before the closing.

Riding the wind and breaking thousands of miles of waves

The game started at 7:00 PM. The opening tip-off was won by the American team, but Lu Zhongsi quickly stole the ball and passed it to Wei Haiqing. Wei, under the basket, hesitated and missed. Kong Guangyi's long shot was also off target. Wei Haiqing redeemed himself and scored the first points, putting the Chinese on the board. The American team was startled, and the US team counterattacked, advancing on all fronts. Hannes took the lead, but Chen Xianglong stopped him, drawing a foul. Hannes converted both free throws, making the score 2-2. Liang Guoquan made a layup under the basket, and Wei Haiqing jumped into the air and scored. The momentum was greatly enhanced, and the Chinese players, riding the wind and breaking thousands of miles of waves, seemed to have the ambition to restore peace to the world.

A wave stirring ten thousand acres

The Chinese team's eight minutes of struggle created a sensation. Like a wave stirring ten thousand acres, a spark could start a prairie fire. The forwards were successful, and the defenders followed up. However, the inside was vulnerable, and the American players invaded. Squier scored, followed by Hannes. The scores of the two teams became equal. At that time, they encouraged each other and fought fiercely. American Smith and Bissell's two goals were like flying generals descending from the sky, catching everyone by surprise. From then on, the Americans steadily improved, while the Chinese could only watch from afar. The score at halftime was 21-14 in favor of the Americans.

The spirit is willing, but the flesh is weak

During the break, the Chinese team's strategist, Jin Hong, secretly gave instructions. As the second half began, they passed the ball three or four times, and Wei Haiqing scored, sending a wave of excitement through the crowd. Some thought that with a good start, it would not be difficult to regain control. However, time passed quickly, and the situation changed abruptly. The American team was well-prepared, and every attack was successful. The Chinese team's spirit was willing, but the flesh was weak. They faced many difficulties and could not move forward. The outcome was already decided, and both sides used their substitutes. In the end, the Americans won 38-27. In summary of the three final games, the Americans won two to one, claiming this year's championship.

Free Talk

World Tidbits 152

--Hai Ke

▲Mrs. Keidel of the United States is 70 years old and suffers from various ailments, but has crossed the Atlantic Ocean 45 times. She is currently in Europe and will embark on a 1,000-mile automobile journey.

▲In 16th-century England, there was a type of spoon called a "Apostle Spoon," which was often given as a gift at baptisms. Today, they have become valuable antiques and fetch high prices at auctions. A set of thirteen spoons from the time of King Henry VIII sold for a staggering 4,900 British pounds.

▲Fishmongers in Paris, knowing that customers prefer red gills on fish, came up with the idea of applying red ink to the gills. One was caught by the police and fined.

▲Four young children in England traveled from Devonport to South Shields to visit their mother. The oldest was only seven, and the youngest was still in swaddling clothes. They traveled 450 miles by train without an escort. Railway staff at major towns along the way provided them with food and treated them specially.

▲There is a large bird in South America called the flamingo. It is as tall as a crane but has a beak like an eagle. They were heavily hunted by the natives of the Bahamas and now only about 1,200 remain. They are now being raised on land developed by the British and Americans.

▲A famous European doctor discovered during the Great War that living nerves from dogs could be transplanted into the bodies of wounded soldiers. Sensation returned in 148 days, and movement was possible in 340 days.

The Death of Fan Fanshan 153

--Chen Yuanliang

The poet Fan Fanshan fell ill in the old capital last autumn and never recovered. Literary enthusiasts were deeply concerned, hoping for a speedy recovery and more of his brilliant works. However, the shocking news arrived that he had passed away due to a stroke at 9:30 PM on March 14th. Literary figures throughout the country must be saddened.

Fan was from Enshi County, Hubei. From a young age, he possessed remarkable talent and a strong family education, so he always excelled in examinations. He studied with the great scholar Li Ciming and gained deep insights. His poetic talent was outstanding, and he could write essays with ease. When Zhang Nanpi was governor-general of the province, he heard of Fan's name and recruited him into his staff. Through long-term influence, Fan's learning advanced even further. After passing the provincial examination, he was promoted to the position of Jinshi (presented scholar). Subsequently, he was appointed as the magistrate of Yichuan County, Shaanxi. Fan was skilled in debate and could resolve cases with a few words, winning the approval of listeners. His judgments and rulings were both solemn and humorous, widely praised. When Ronglu was in power, he invited Fan to join his staff and assist in strategy for some time. When the Boxer Rebellion broke out, Fan followed the emperor during the crisis. Later, the reform edicts of Empress Dowager Cixi were entirely written by him. At that time, Fan's prominence was at its peak, which aroused jealousy, leading to his dismissal. The following year, he was reappointed as the Jiangning Treasurer. At that time, Duanfang was the governor-general of Liangjiang. In his spare time, he often enjoyed discussing ancient and modern events with Fan. When the revolutionary army rose and Nanjing fell, Fan fled to Shanghai, closed his doors to study, and did not ask about worldly affairs. He once wore a Taoist robe, took a picture, and wrote a poem on it, which included the line, "If the court asks about Tao Hongjing, the pine breeze in June cools my pillow and mat," showing it to friends to express his determination. Li Yuanhong recommended him as the Minister of Civil Affairs, but he refused. Yuan Shikai also admired his talent and treated him with great respect, but he only reluctantly accepted the position of advisor. Fan was honest and upright as an official. Although he held a prominent position, he remained poor. Therefore, his funeral was arranged by his close friends, Li Shikang and others. He left behind a widow, a daughter-in-law, and two grandsons, and their situation was quite desolate. However, he left behind a wealth of writings, including published collections of poetry, ci poetry, prose, political essays, official documents, and notes. Among them, poetry was the most abundant, with about 20,000 unpublished poems. He truly deserves to be called a poet of his generation. His official documents were widely circulated and praised, and legal scholars regarded them as models. In his later years, Fan devoted himself to pleasures. Whenever he was at banquets, surrounded by beautiful women, his poetic inspiration would surge, and good lines would flow like pearls. He particularly liked opera, focusing on the roles of female impersonators. When Mei Lanfang first created the "Goddess Scattering Flowers" opera, Fan wrote poems to praise him, filled with enchanting and warm affection. As for actresses such as Xin Yanqiu, Rong Lijuan, Meng Lijun, Liu Yanqin, Xiao Lanfen, and the Ma sisters, Yanyun and Yanqiu, almost all became famous with his support. Now that he has passed away, it is conceivable that those actresses will also frown and express their sorrow.

The Origin of Horse Racing 154

--Lu Bing

Every spring and autumn, horse races are held in Shanghai. The racetrack is filled with men and women, and skilled jockeys get the chance to show off their skills. The practice of horse racing has ancient origins, with a history of about five thousand years. In the past, monarchs raised horses for racing and entertainment, not for the general public.

Recent archaeological discoveries in the Mesopotamian plains have revealed that the earliest horse races did not originate in Europe but in Asia. The Hittite people of Asia Minor were very fond of this activity. According to records, this was more than 1,000 years before the Common Era. The records detail the methods of training horses before major races. Professor Hou Langxi of Borago University made a detailed study of the findings and learned that although the people of that time were not fully civilized, they were advanced in the field of horse racing. This is truly remarkable. They paid attention to the horses' diet, ensuring that they were not overweight. They also bathed the horses frequently to ensure balanced development. The training methods were methodical, progressing from slow walks to fast runs, and the methods used were indeed excellent. It is also stated that the period from the start of training to the race was about six months.

An Interview at Mr. Zhang Yuguang's Studio 155

— Wu Jiren

It has been a year since I left Shanghai. At the beginning of this month, I returned to the city by the sea. I visited the renowned painter Mr. Zhang Yuguang at his residence, "Yezhou Studio," on Xietu Road. I also presented him with over ten rare goldfish as a birthday gift. This was because Mr. Zhang and I share a refined hobby. Yezhou Studio consists of three rooms, located in the center of a garden. The garden spans about two to three acres and is densely planted with flowers and trees. Two grape trellises extend for several lengths. It is a pity that the early spring snow damaged the buds and leaves. Otherwise, the beautiful garden would be even more inviting. To the right of the studio is a pool of spring water, with weeping willows gently touching the ground, creating a serene and secluded scene. On the side of the garden, there is a statue of the revolutionary hero Zhao Sheng, about ten feet tall, imposing and magnificent, worthy of being a great figure of his era. I asked Mr. Zhang about it, and he informed me that it was originally made for Jingkou Park and this was the remaining plaster model. Inside the studio, the walls are adorned with a dazzling array of works, including pastel drawings, oil paintings, charcoal drawings, watercolors, brush paintings, and ink sketches. All are copied from Western works and ancient originals, or blend Chinese and Western styles into one. Original creations make up the majority. They are all so perfect that a young novice like myself dares not comment on them. Mr. Zhang quickly offered me a seat and asked about my life in the countryside, showing much appreciation. Although I am not a refined scholar, I am naturally proud and unwilling to follow the crowd. I admire Mr. Zhang for making a living through art, avoiding dependence on others. However, I fear my imitation will only be a superficial attempt. Later, we discussed contemporary figures and Mr. Zhang's past contributions to the revolution in his younger years. Mr. Zhang said, "During that period, I assisted Yu Youren in running the 'Min Li,' 'Min Hu,' and 'Min Xu' newspapers, tirelessly promoting the revolution. Time has passed, and I am now old and unable to contribute much. As for important figures in the party and the nation, such as my old friends Wang Zhengting and Ye Chucang, my close friend Niu Tiesheng, and my wife's younger brother Jing Hengyi, they are still working diligently for the country. I, on the other hand, have devoted myself to painting and immersed myself in art. I no longer have the heroic spirit of those years." He sighed as he spoke. It was past noon, and I bid farewell. Mr. Zhang insisted on me staying for lunch, which I could not refuse. Soon, Mr. Zhang's wife, Ms. Huang, returned. After being introduced, I learned that she had been working at the local detention center for many years, being a pioneer in women's participation in politics. Ms. Huang was very kind and did not have the common habits of the time, which was admirable. After a satisfying meal, I returned home and wrote this account.

▲ Short News: The Cantonese singer and dancer Ms. Zi Luolan recently performed at the National Grand Theater in the capital, with daily ticket sales exceeding 2,000 yuan. Gifts from important figures in the party and the nation numbered in the hundreds. The Capital Cinema intended to invite Ms. Zi Luolan to continue her performances. However, Mr. Luo Mingyou of Lianhua Film Company invited her to Tianjin. She departed on the Jinpu train on the 20th. After arriving in Tianjin, she will perform at the Guangming Grand Theater for three days, then go to Beijing to perform at the Zhenguang, Ping An, and Mingxing theaters. She is expected to return to Shanghai in about a month to fulfill her contract with Lianhua Film Company to make a sound film. Many venues in Suzhou, Hangzhou, and other places have also invited her to perform. (Jia)

▲ Correction Regarding Guyi Garden: In the article about Guyi Garden published on March 20th, there were some errors. Guyi Garden was built by the great painter Li Liufang of the Ming Dynasty, known as the "Old Man of Tanyuan." The garden is known for its square bamboo, a special product. The inscription was written by Dong Qichang, also a Ming Dynasty person. The original article mistakenly stated that he was from the Qing Dynasty. This correction is made. (Shan Ruo)

China's "All Quiet on the Western Front" 156

— Zheng Kangmin

"All Quiet on the Western Front" is a world-renowned novel. Recently, it has been translated into multiple versions in our country and made into a film. The Chinese people have almost universally welcomed this kind of famous work depicting war. However, looking back at our own country's novels, there is a lack of such grand creations depicting war, which is truly regrettable. Recently, I heard about the emergence of a great war novel. People in literary circles are excitedly spreading the news. The author is said to be Mr. Huang Zhenxia, who was once widely reported to have died in battle at Guide. Mr. Huang has returned from the battlefield and completed "On the Longhai Line." He vividly depicts life on the front lines, the true face of war, the situation of charging into battle, and the psychology of soldiers. It is comparable to Remarque's "All Quiet on the Western Front." However, Remarque's work has a foreign flavor, creating a gap with the psychology of Chinese readers. Mr. Huang's "On the Longhai Line" is truly a local scene, like vegetables that taste best when grown in one's own garden. I predict that Mr. Huang's work will become a bestseller, as popular as Remarque's.

What kind of person is Mr. Huang? Readers should remember that this newspaper's "Art World" section often published his poems and essays. His concise writing style and beautiful diction left a deep impression on people. Mr. Huang's ancestral home is in eastern Guangdong, but he grew up in Shanghai. He lost his father at a young age, and his mother also died of appendicitis last year. Feeling lonely and overwhelmed with sorrow, he indulged in alcohol and women every day. North Sichuan Road is known as a mysterious street in Shanghai. Whenever the moon rose, he would walk alone there, sometimes venturing into dance halls to dance wildly under the lights. This was also due to the unspeakable pain in his life. Later, rumors spread among his friends that Mr. Huang had disappeared, which seemed bizarre. People scrambled to inquire about him. Within a month, they learned from Mr. Huang's close friends that he had enlisted in the Central Army when it was recruiting new soldiers at the North Station. From then on, he abandoned his pen and joined the army, emulating Ban Dingyuan's heroic deeds. Letters were exchanged from time to time. Later, he was admitted to the Central Military Academy. When the news came, his friends celebrated with great joy, marking this day as Mr. Huang's rebirth. When Yan Feng raised troops in rebellion, the Central Army was deployed to the front lines. Mr. Huang was able to participate as a recruit from the Central Military Academy. Then, correspondence ceased. During the battle of Guide, our army showed a determination to fight to the death, suffering heavy losses. Mr. Huang's fate was uncertain, and there was no news of him. All those who knew or did not know Mr. Huang sighed with sorrow, believing that there was no chance of survival in the chaos of battle. This newspaper's "Art World" section, as well as the "Vanguard Weekly" and "Vanguard Monthly," all published memorial articles one after another. Who knew that events are impermanent and news is not always accurate? After the military situation was settled and the overall situation stabilized, our army returned in triumph. It was then that people learned that Mr. Huang was still alive. Friends were overjoyed upon hearing this good news. Upon his return, Mr. Huang first visited Mr. Zhu Yingpeng. He was overjoyed to have survived the battlefield. At that time, he spoke eloquently and recounted the details of the battle. He then presented his work titled "On the Longhai Line," which was comprehensive and detailed. After polishing the manuscript, it felt even more vivid to read. It is truly the greatest achievement of the Chinese literary world. The local flavor is extremely rich, such as the steepness of Yejigang and the suffering of the people in the war zone, the scene of being displaced. Mr. Huang uses his ingenious pen to make readers feel as if they are in a war-torn environment. Calling it China's "All Quiet on the Western Front" is not an exaggeration. It is said that this work will be published in the Modern Bookstore's "Vanguard Monthly" No. 5. In addition to "On the Longhai Line," his poem "The Qin and the Sword" will also be published in the same issue.

Travels in India (4) 157

— Linghua

On the morning of the 23rd, I visited various bookstores. I saw countless English books written by Indians themselves. Their academic and cultural wealth surpasses that of our country. Very few people in our country can write in English, while various Indian philosophies are translated into English in abundance. Observing Tagore's world cultural and artistic movement, one knows that Western culture has been greatly influenced by Indian culture. China today is greatly lacking in contributions to world culture, almost to the point of being insignificant. In the prosperous Han and Tang dynasties, after the world was settled, culture and education were promoted. All the more so should we do that in this age of international communication. While talking with an Indian, I learned that the Japanese Iroha alphabet, created by the monk Kukai, was based on Indian phonetics. Therefore, many Japanese sounds add the "a" sound. Today, Indians also pronounce many sounds in this way. Therefore, when Indians mix their native pronunciation with English, their English sounds very different from Chinese pronunciation.

Indian universities now have Indian history courses. But Mr. Xinhan told me that Indian concepts are very different from those of the Chinese. Indians do not pay attention to the history of kings but pay the most attention to religious sects and academics. Therefore, there is no history of kings. Because Indian culture has been around for a long time, little of it can be verified. Clear history only began after the death of the Buddha, during the reign of King Ashoka, around 200 BC. The rest are myths, speculations, and fragmented and difficult to count. According to my reading of the famous Indian work Gita, the history of its earliest transmission began with "The Great MahabbarataWar3ioi, BC." I imagine it should be around 3101 BC. It has been about 5,000 years since then, so the length of its generations can be known. According to the Gita, Hinduism originated 5,000 years ago, more than 2,000 years before the Buddha, and it has not declined to this day. It is prevalent in India, which is also a spectacle. It is something that should be studied.

Dr. Mahondranath came to visit and inquired about Chinese Taoism. He invited me to his home. I briefly described the situation of Chinese culture. His students listened quietly by his side. Dr. Mohan said that he hoped for the progress of China's national power and the promotion of its culture, which he would strive to spread. He is a famous professor of philosophy at Sumkrit College, Senga Lee University. I asked him about Western philosophy, but he didn't seem to care about it. The Indian philosophy history translated by Westerners that I read admits that Indian philosophy is complex and profound, beyond the comprehension of most people in the world. Today, Indians still claim to be in the highest position in philosophy. In terms of spiritual culture, they not only hold the reins of Asia but also want to be in a guiding position in the world. Tagore has the title of "Poet Saint," and Gandhi is also called "Mahatma." Even in prison, he is not a prisoner. Judges address him as "Mahatma" and salute him before speaking. In addition, the World Buddhist Association and the Asian Women's Association convened by Indians will open next year. I heard that the Asian Art Association is being convened now.

Flour Market: Difficult to Recover 167

Yesterday, the flour market saw a downtrend across all months. Although foreign wheat prices fluctuated, overall sentiment considered both domestic and foreign flour and wheat still to be in a period of oversupply. It was rumored that despite large shipments of American wheat seeking sales in China, foreign firms were only quoting four taels, requiring orders of no less than 50,000 tons each time. Moreover, yesterday's quoted price for Canadian flour remained only $1.27. With such pressure, the inability of sentiment to recover was understandable. As of this month, spot prices in Tianjin have also fallen sharply, from $3.12 to $3.07-08. Consequently, if gold prices fall further, the distant months may even drop to 9.5 qian. As a result, this month fell 1.5 fen compared to the previous day. April and May fell 1 fen, June and July fell 1.5 fen, and August fell 0.5 li.

Futures Wheat: Rise and Subsequent Weakening 168

Yesterday, the futures wheat market initially showed positive signs after opening in the morning. This month is approaching delivery, and due to substandard foreign wheat arrivals, dealers such as Tai Kang and Ding Tai were unable to meet their upgrade requirements and had to cover their positions and ship spot goods to Hankou. Consequently, sentiment improved. Distant months also saw short covering and price hikes, rising approximately 2 to 3 fen compared to the previous day. The results were unchanged for this month, up 1 fen for April, up 2 fen for May, up 1 fen for June, and down 1 fen for July and August.

Yesterday, Fair SSS sold for 4 taels, Tian You 1000 series remained at 4.55 taels, 2000 series at 4.6 taels, and Tian Feng brand at 4.325 taels.

North-South Goods: Wood Ear Fungus Rebounds in Hankou 174

The lowest-priced offer for wood ear fungus in Hankou was as low as 130 taels for top-grade fungus and 74-75 taels for mixed fungus. According to letters, sales have gradually increased recently, and the trend has turned bullish. Sub-grade fungus has rebounded by 10 taels, reaching 140 taels, and mixed fungus has risen to 80 taels. Even at this price, it is still inverted compared to Shanghai prices. Therefore, local merchants lack interest in buying. Looking back at the Shanghai market, ordinary mixed fungus does not exceed 90 taels, and sub-grade fungus is only 155 taels. Based on local prices, everyone would incur losses.

Silk and Tea: Continued Shipments of Tin Factory Silk to Shanghai 175

As the end of March approaches, Wuxi manufacturers are preparing to deliver this month's futures silk sold to foreign firms. Therefore, manufacturers are shipping batches of silk to Shanghai. Yesterday, the Xihu passenger train transported 130 pieces of White Factory Silk from brands such as Golden Double Deer and Golden Double Eagle to Shanghai in preparation for the end-of-month delivery to foreign firms. The local foreign firm silk market remains unchanged. Exchange rates have stabilized, and foreign Shanghai White Factory Silk telegrams show a small increase in prices. However, factories are holding firm, unwilling to sell due to continued large losses. Market sentiment is weak. Yesterday, only Xinfu shipped 10 bales of White Factory Silk to Shanghai, and Dachang and others shipped 20 bales of Sichuan Yellow Factory Silk. Prices remain weak.

Youth Forum

Fudan Photography Society and the Fudan Photography Yearbook 176

— Xi Jia

I dare say that, among the student-run photography groups in schools, the Fudan Photography Society is perhaps one of the most complete and spirited. This is not only the opinion of some people, but also the praise from the Hua She group, who are commonly recognized as the first-class photographers in China. Indeed, the Fudan Photography Society has a considerable position in society. The creation of this position is due to the three sensational photography exhibitions.

The founding of the Fudan Photography Society dates back to 1928. After a year of training, the first photography exhibition was held. The following year, the second exhibition was realized. Last year, the third exhibition, held at the same time as the 25th anniversary of Fudan University, provided most of the material selected for this Fudan Photography Yearbook.

In recent years, many photographic talents have emerged, and their works have spread to newspapers across the country. People who are slightly concerned about photography have also gained a considerable understanding of the Fudan Photography Society.

During this third exhibition, it was held on the same day as the 25th anniversary celebration, which made a very deep impression on people. Therefore, after the exhibition, various newspapers and pictorial magazines clamored for the publication of Fudan photography works. This is a fact.

However, the people of the Photography Society cannot be complacent, believing that they cannot provide people with a permanent opportunity to browse. Therefore, there is a desire to publish the Fudan Photography Yearbook.

I heard that the "Fudan Photography Yearbook" is already available for pre-sale. It is said that the content includes not only the best works from the third exhibition but also works from the first and second exhibitions. Then its results will be more fulfilling.

Regarding photo collections, I have seen many of them. I can say that none of the ones published in China are perfect. It is said that the copperplates for the Fudan Photography Yearbook are entirely made by the American Engraving Company. As for the printing and paper, they are certainly very exquisite.

In short, within a school, it is already difficult to organize a complete photography society, let alone hold an exhibition every year, and even more difficult to publish a photography collection. However, the Fudan Photography Society has been able to do it all. This not only makes us very admirable but also makes us yearn for it.

Now that the yearbook is about to be published, I hope that all beauty lovers in the world will have a copy in hand so as not to let down this great "Fudan Photography Yearbook" that is worth appreciating.

Book and Newspaper Introductions

Youth of the Era — Issue 29 177

— Zuo

In China today, an era of suffering, nothing is perfect. Taking the publishing industry as an example, booksellers only know how to cater to social psychology, disregarding distorted facts to accelerate production, using crudely made, trashy books to extract (plunder) money from young people. But many young people are still willing to be deceived by them.

Indeed, young people are too pitiful. Besides the dry and boring school textbooks, it is really difficult to find two suitable extracurricular reading materials. Apart from the crudely made, trashy books and newspapers distributed by booksellers, what other books and newspapers are available for reading? It is as difficult as ascending to heaven to find a publication that speaks for the youth themselves or books and newspapers that can defend the youth and negate aspects of themselves.

However, young people need not be too disappointed, because the "Youth of the Era" published by the Youth of the Era Society has solved the above-mentioned problem for us. As you can see, the new opening statement in issue 27 of the publication clearly explains:

"We cannot be content with the status quo and hope to express the spirit of the youth of our era, allowing our minds to grasp the comfort of the right path. As a result, we finally lift our heads from the constraints of the low-pressure atmosphere and move forward on the path of struggle."

Therefore, "Youth of the Era" will become a must-read publication for the youth of the era. The publication has been published for more than half a year. Originally, it was in the form of single sheets, with in-depth discussions on the theory and practice of the youth movement. Since issue 27, it has been changed to a book format, and the content has become more substantial and impressive. It is hoped that every youth of the era should pay special attention to it. Here are my recommendations for the recently published issue 29:

The content of this issue includes Bing's "Our Understanding of Electing Representatives to the National Assembly," Ping Ren's "Dynamic Research and Static Research," Yi Shun's "On Coeducation," Dian Zhi's "Casual Talks on Youth Reading Materials," Xu Ze Xiang's "Awakening from a Dream," and Xu Xia's "A Day of Crazy Wandering," etc. Both in terms of quality and quantity, this issue has made significant progress compared to previous issues. The editors of the publication said,

"This is the third time our publication has met with readers since the reorganization to this issue. In terms of quantity, it can be said to have increased somewhat in these three issues after the reorganization. But in terms of quality, we are not clever self-aware individuals, so we dare not make definitive statements. We are willing to let readers do this work. At the same time, we hope that readers who love our publication will often give us corrections and instructions, so that we can use them as guidelines and compasses." Precisely because I am a reader, I will therefore make a judgment on the quality. Although it may not be able to serve as a guideline and compass for the publication, it can at least make some contribution to the youth who are seeking good reading materials.

Bing's "Our Understanding of Electing Representatives to the National Assembly" is the most noteworthy article. With the National Assembly about to open and various regions conducting elections for representatives, this issue should not only be understood by young people, but also by everyone else. The author said, "In order to express the ability of us young people who are fighting for the national movement and who feel more keenly than anyone else,

we must have careful and precise consideration and exploration when electing representatives to the National Assembly this time. We must not resolutely regard it as a blind following without any pain or itching. We must abandon all distracting thoughts, take out the spirit of impartiality and selflessness, and elect a truly worthy leader of our youth to be our representative in this National Assembly, which is responsible for such a great mission and for solving national affairs and advancing politics." Who says it isn't so?

Ping Ren's "Dynamic Research and Static Research" is a reading method written based on facts and experience. He said that the goals of research have two directions: static and dynamic.

Using these two research methods to study can achieve the following effects:

Continued on Page 9

Page 22

Page 23

Continued from Page 7

Excellent results: (1) It prevents feeling bored during research and losing interest in studying academic subjects. (2) In-depth research into two academic subjects often leads to the same path, while also helping the progress of the other academic subject. (3) When leaving school and entering society in the future, the scope of such application is relatively broad and the opportunities for application are also many. (4) It can achieve a shortcut to specialized research in the future, which is much more practical than the currently popular plaster-selling so-called "learning methods of various subjects," without any empty drawbacks and indeed can be used as a reference for young people's reading.

"On Coeducation" is written by Yi Shun, who elucidates from an objective standpoint, from the historical, biological, sociological, and school perspectives, that coeducation is of great benefit to mankind, society, morality, education, temperament, and everything else, and is enough to be a wake-up call for those who are confused.

Mo Zhi's "Casual Talks on Youth Reading Materials" has a profound review of China's publishing industry today. After reading the section recorded below, one can know that this article has considerable value.

"Finally, it must be understood that the reading materials needed by our modern youth are by no means so simple, a kind of vulgar works that tend to be commercialized. In terms of knowledge and learning, they cannot make us spend our parents' blood and sweat and get considerable results. Reading such books really has no value at all. However, young people are being fooled by these booksellers (or merchants). I subjectively say a practical word, the reading materials we young people need now are practical and concrete texts that help academic progress. Those mysterious and incorrect things are not needed in the present. The most important thing is that the pricing should be particularly low. Do not be hypocritical, on the one hand, shouting to reduce the burden on readers, on the other hand, selling the books except for the highest actual price, and then according to the so-called "peer agreement, add one according to the code" money-making trick, money is certainly to be earned, but do not consign the deeply burdened mission of promoting culture to the Yellow Sea. This can also be said to be a proverb given by the youth to the new book industry."

In addition, Xu Ze Xiang's "Awakening from a Dream" and Shu Xia's "A Day of Crazy Wandering," both literary works, express the unique emotions of young people. The former is a poem with generous and impassioned calls, and the latter can be said to be a short story, although the author lists it as the second of Random Notes on White Snow. Because it is written in the first person, the material expressed is more thorough and deep.

Finally, there is also a collection of school radio reports, reporting the news of various schools, which young people probably all like to watch.

In addition, the publication is published by the Youth of the Era Society at 210 Fangxie Road, Ximen, and each issue only sells for three cents, which is indeed a good reading material with low price and high quality that best suits the tastes of young people. I hope young people will not ignore it.

Manuscript Guidelines for Book and Newspaper Introductions 178

(1) The text is limited to introducing new publications in China and abroad. In addition to literary works, all political, economic, legal, scientific, educational, etc. books and newspapers are included in the introduction, but boring books and newspapers will not be introduced.

(2) The pictures are limited to recent works by new domestic and foreign artists and attached pictures related to the text.

(3) Manuscripts regarding textual research or research on ancient Chinese books will not be published.

(4) Pictures and photos are limited to those related to the text.

(5) Each text should not exceed 3,000 characters.

(6) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(7) Do not use blue ink or colored paper for pictures, use white paper and black ink.

(8) Please indicate on the manuscript that it is a [newspaper] introduction.

(9) Whether the manuscript is published or not, it will not be returned. If you need to return it, please declare it in advance and attach sufficient postage.

(10) Remuneration for texts is divided into three types: three yuan, two yuan, and one yuan per thousand characters. The same applies to pictures and photos. If there are special manuscripts, remuneration will be calculated separately.

(11) Remuneration for texts is divided into three types: three yuan, two yuan, and one yuan per thousand characters. The same applies to each picture and photo. If there are special manuscripts, remuneration will be calculated separately.
